Local News

Belgian Envoy Baron Guillaume Returns Home Yesterday; Mayor Wu and Others Personally Went to the Port to Bid Farewell

According to New Sound News Agency, Belgian Ambassador to China Baron Guillaume's term has expired. Yesterday morning at 10:00 AM, he departed Shanghai aboard the Java Company's ship "Tjipatti," along with his wife and children, to return to his country via the Dutch East Indies. Mr. and Mrs. Guillaume arrived at the New Customs Wharf at 8:30 AM, took a ferry to the Pootung Blue Funnel Wharf, and transferred to the "Tjipatti."

Those seeing them off included:

Mayor of this city, Wu Tiecheng, who personally went to the New Customs Wharf with his secretary, Tang Shixuan, to see them off. In addition, those who went to the ship to bid farewell included Chen Bingzhang, representing Vice Premier of the Executive Yuan and Minister of Finance Kong Xiangxi; Zhou Jue, Director of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs Office in Shanghai; Lu Bohong; and Consul Tanerfu, Counselor of the Belgian Embassy and Consul General in Shanghai; Cheng Yinglin, Secretary of the Consulate; Hers, Chairman of the Belgian Chamber of Commerce; Lambert, General Manager of Banque Belge Pour L'Etranger, Far East; Lafond, Manager of the Shanghai branch; Peng Tuo, Director of Banque Franco-Chinoise; Strode, a well-known Belgian arms dealer; and more than twenty other people. Ambassador Guillaume had previously visited Minister Kong to bid farewell. Mr. Kong returned the visit the night before and learned that the Belgian government had awarded Mr. Kong the highest medal. The telegram arrived in Shanghai yesterday, and Ambassador Guillaume notified Mr. Kong and offered his congratulations.

Remarks Before Departure

Before his departure, Ambassador Guillaume told the New Sound News Agency reporter at the port, "I have stayed in China for six and a half years (previously incorrectly reported as three and a half years). This time, I am returning to my country. Whether I will come to China again depends on the orders of the government, which has not yet been decided. I have traveled to various places before and have been deeply impressed. I feel that your country has made a lot of progress, especially in terms of construction. I am very reluctant to leave China this time." When Mr. Guillaume said this, the reporter asked about the upgrading of the Chinese and Belgian envoys. He replied, "This matter has not been decided yet. I have not had any contact with your country. Perhaps the Chinese Ambassador to Belgium, Mr. Zhu (Hexiang), has had contact here, but I don't know. However, this matter is very likely to be realized." The reporter then asked about the Belgian loan for the Longhai Railway. Ambassador Guillaume said, "This is a long-standing issue that has been completely resolved about a month ago. As for the details of the resolution, I regret that I cannot tell you." Ambassador Guillaume also stated that after his departure, the embassy's affairs will be temporarily handled by Mr. Tanerfu. The trip to the Dutch East Indies is purely for travel. He will stay there for a few days and then transfer to another ship to return to Europe.

Belgian Ambassador Guillaume and his wife

Lottery for Redemption of Principal for Three Types of Unified Finance and Telecommunications Bonds Held Yesterday Morning; Total Redemption of Principal is 2,175,000 Yuan; Unified Bonds Payable at the End of January Next Year, Balance at the End of the Month

The second time for the Type B bonds of the 25th Year of the Republic Unified Public Bonds, the sixth time for the 17th Year of the Republic Financial Long-Term Public Bonds, and the fourth time for the 24th Year of the Republic Telecommunications Public Bonds, for the lottery of redemption of principal, were held yesterday morning at 10:00 AM at the Bankers' Association on Hong Kong Road. Tao Changshan, Director of the Public Debt Department of the Ministry of Finance, was present. Lin Jinyu, Supervisor of the Auditing Department. Xu Jiqin of the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce. Li Fusun of the Bankers' Association. Shen Jingliang of the Money Dealers' Association. Fan Jietang of the National Debt Fund Custody Committee. Lottery members Jin Wenyuan of the Central Bank. Zhu Qizhen of the Bank of China. Chen Mutang of the Bank of Communications. and more than forty other people. A total of thirty-three lots were drawn for the redemption of principal, totaling 2,175,000 yuan, which was completed at 12:00 PM. The details are recorded as follows:

Chairman's Report

Chairman of the Public Debt Department reported that today is the lottery for the redemption of principal of the three types of public bonds, namely the 25th Year of the Republic Unified Public Bonds Type B and others. The lottery method, except for the Telecommunications Public Bonds which use the last two digits of the number, both the Unified Public Bonds Type B and the Financial Long-Term Public Bonds use the last three digits of the number. Now, I will briefly report to you the situation of each bond. (1) The 25th Year of the Republic Unified Public Bonds Type B was issued in February of the 25th Year of the Republic, with a fixed amount of 150 million national currency. The principal has already been redeemed once, and this is the second redemption. Five lots will be drawn, each with 150,000 yuan, totaling 750,000 yuan. (2) The 17th Year of the Republic Financial Long-Term Public Bonds was issued in November of the 17th Year of the Republic, with a total amount of 45 million yuan. The principal has already been redeemed five times, and this is the sixth redemption. Twenty-five lots will be drawn, each with 45,000 yuan, totaling 1,125,000 yuan. (3) The 24th Year of the Republic Telecommunications Public Bonds was issued in September of the 24th Year of the Republic, with a total amount of 10 million yuan. The principal has already been redeemed three times, and this is the fourth redemption. Three lots will be drawn, each with 100,000 yuan, totaling 300,000 yuan. The principal and accrued interest for the above-mentioned bonds will be paid by the Central, China, and Communications Banks in various places starting from September 30th, except for the Financial Long-Term Public Bonds and the Telecommunications Public Bonds. The Unified Public Bonds Type B will be paid by the Central Bank and its entrusted China and Communications Banks and the Central Trust Bureau in various places starting from January 31st of the 26th year. In order to facilitate the financing of bondholders, those who hold the winning bonds of the Unified Public Bonds Type B and the interest coupons due at the end of January of the 26th year may discount them at the China and Communications Banks and rediscount them at the Central Bank. The Ministry has issued letters to the three banks on February 15th of the 25th year to check and handle this matter and combine the report. Now, please ask the supervisors to check the lottery tickets and the lottery ticket register for the execution of the lottery.

Western Newspaper Reports that Sino-French Airmail Must Have Sufficient Airmail Stamps and Specify Routing via Hanoi

According to the North China Daily News, starting from the beginning of September, there will be airmail transported from Shanghai to Guangzhou every week. Starting from the 9th, the direct air route to France will also be started. The method is that on Tuesdays, Thursdays, Saturdays and Sundays, the aircraft of China National Aviation Corporation will transport the mail from Shanghai to Guangzhou, then Southwest Aviation Corporation will transport it from Guangzhou to Hanoi, and then Air France will transport it from Hanoi to France. This airmail service was started a few months ago, but was suspended due to a dispute between China National Aviation Corporation and Southwest Aviation Corporation over which party's aircraft should transport the mail from Guangzhou to Hanoi, and then the Guangdong-Guangxi incident. Yesterday, Huang, Deputy Postal Director of the Maritime District, told the North China Daily News representative that this accident no longer exists, so the air transport will be resumed from today. Recently, some people have criticized that the mail between Guangzhou and Hanoi is often transported by ship. This is indeed the case, but it is due to the bad weather. One aircraft was delayed and could not connect with another aircraft that was scheduled to depart. Rather than waiting for two days for the next aircraft to arrive, it is better to hand it over to the ship for transportation as soon as possible, but this is only done occasionally. The new business allows French postal letters to be transported to Shanghai within twelve days. All airmail destined for France or European cities, whether letters, postcards, or printed matter (including newspapers), must pay an additional 6.5 cents for every five centimeters in addition to the usual postage stamps. Those exceeding five centimeters must pay an additional 6.5 cents. However, those sent to Greece and Italy only need to pay six cents for every five centimeters. These mails must specify "Routing via Hanoi" on the surface. Mr. Huang also said that all airmail sent to Shanghai and other cities in China from foreign countries that have paid sufficient airmail postage will be transported by air, as well as mail transported by Air France or Imperial Airways to Hong Kong. Mail transported to Hong Kong will first be transported by train to Guangzhou, and then transported by aircraft of China National Aviation Corporation. As for those who only pay the airmail postage to Hanoi or Hong Kong, they will be transported by ordinary postal routes.

Soviet Ambassador Hosts Talk with the Press Yesterday

According to TASS News Agency, Shanghai, September 10th, Soviet Ambassador to China, Bogomolov, hosted a talk with representatives of the Chinese and foreign press in this city on a wooden morning, and made the following remarks:

"A few days ago, I met with Chinese newspaper reporters in Nanjing and resolutely refuted the malicious rumors of the German news agency, such as the "famine" in Ukraine, the conflict between farmers and the army, etc. The interview from Ukrainian Acting People's Commissar of Agriculture, Gukhevsky, which was published in several Chinese newspapers a few days ago, has proven with figures that these slanders are purely fabricated. I am very pleased that the Chinese newspapers published the above interview. Only one thing is true in the interview, that by the end of this year, no farmer in Ukraine will be without his own cow, which is sufficient to prove the great achievements of agricultural development and improve the living standards of the people.

"Gentlemen, you may recall that the German news agency once spread the message that the Chairman of the Council of People's Commissars, Molotov, had resigned, and unfortunately, many Chinese newspapers also published it. However, Mr. Mo actually represented the Soviet government to review a parade on the Red Square after his "resignation," which is not a strange story. I must point out that the local Japanese newspapers are still echoing and continuing the anti-Soviet propaganda launched by the German news agency. In order to make this kind of false news contain local significance, they have rumored that our military attaché, Mr. Repin, "does not agree with the policy of the Soviet government and was recalled." At the same time, the press also rumored that Repin had been placed in the bottom cabin of the 'Sefuer' ship and 'escorted' to Vladivostok.

"However, gentlemen, now you see that the so-called 'escort' does not prevent Mr. Repin from sitting at the same table with us.

"The local Japanese newspapers are very unhappy about the fact that Soviet films are increasingly popular with the Chinese people, but I do not agree with this view. I think this fact is not only beneficial to the Soviet Union and China, but also has great benefits for the entire future of peace.

"The Soviet Union's foreign policy is entirely based on the sole desire to strengthen the peaceful relations between the Soviet Union and other countries. From this, we can understand the efforts we strive to implement this goal in all human activities.

"We believe that one of the main reasons for governments to trap people into war is that the people of that country fail to fully understand the feelings and thoughts of the people of neighboring countries. People will never be willing to endure war, and this fact further proves that cultural communication between the people of all countries can only further develop the friendly relations between the people, and to a certain extent, can prevent the government from organizing any war and conflict. I am personally very pleased that our cultural activities have received the support of the Chinese government and the Chinese people. "Unfortunately, I must declare that the current development of the international situation is very unfavorable. The threat of war has become increasingly urgent. One of the main reasons for this unfavorable development is undoubtedly the policies of certain countries and their governments. These policies are not based on the desire for world peace like the Soviet Union, but on attempts to expand territory and conquer other countries and peoples. Although the facts in recent years have shown the superficial success of this policy, I am convinced that it will eventually collapse, because the victory of this policy will be equivalent to the destruction of mankind.

"I think it is not an exaggeration to say that today's world is standing at a crossroads. One of the crossroads is the road of national narrow-mindedness, national hatred, and the self-mutilation of the people. The second is the road of promoting international coordination, fighting for peace, and fighting for the prosperity of human culture. I am convinced that after the completion of this great goal, the accompanying ones will be the unprecedented prosperity of culture and the well-being of all nations, and the achievement of this goal must be achieved by the leaders and representatives of all peoples, united and jointly fighting against those who attempt to use various ethnic and national elite 'theories' to base their inhuman activities on peace destroyers and war instigators.

Shanghai Municipal Council (SMC) Police File Suit Against Ta Kung Pao for Publishing "A Play That Cannot Be Performed" in the Literary Section; Court Hearing Held Yesterday, Verdict Scheduled for the 17th

Central News Agency reports: The Shanghai Municipal Council (SMC) Police recently sued Zhang Jiluan, editor-in-chief of Ta Kung Pao, in the First Special District Court on charges of disturbing public order. Yesterday was the scheduled hearing date. Mr. Zhang, who was on vacation and traveling, returned from his journey upon receiving the news and appeared in court on time. The trial took place in the Second Court. First, the presiding judge questioned the defendant about his name, age, and origin. Then, the police lawyer stood up to state the grounds for the prosecution, saying that on August 16th, Ta Kung Pao published an article titled "A Play That Cannot Be Performed." The police believed that it contained elements of inciting others to resist lawful orders and, therefore, prosecuted the defendant under Article 153, Section 2 of the Criminal Code. The judge then questioned the defendant. Mr. Zhang stated several points: (1) He is responsible for editing Ta Kung Pao; (2) Ta Kung Pao has always been extremely cautious regarding opinions and news reporting; (3) Novels and dramas published in the literary section and supplements of the newspaper are for entertainment purposes; (4) The article in question is a play script and does not incite others to commit crimes; (5) He has been frequently ill recently and may not have paid sufficient attention to the editing of the supplements. However, he did not know what specific part of the play the police lawyer claimed incited others to resist lawful orders. The judge further inquired about the source of the script. Mr. Zhang replied that it was a submission and he did not know the author's name. At this point, the debate began. The police lawyer continued to explain that the reason he believed the defendant had violated Article 153, Section 2 of the Criminal Code was due to the fact that the National Government issued a decree on maintaining friendly relations with neighboring countries on June 10th of last year. The article "A Play That Cannot Be Performed" incited emotions against the Three Northeastern Provinces and repeatedly mentioned "Manchukuo," which contradicted the decree on maintaining friendly relations. The defendant then asked the judge to allow him to state his views, roughly saying that the newspaper has always paid attention to and respected laws and regulations in its opinions and reporting regarding maintaining friendly relations with neighboring countries. However, he believed that the police lawyer's claim of violating the decree on maintaining friendly relations, based on the mention of the Three Northeastern Provinces and "Manchukuo" in the article, was a misunderstanding. He emphasized that the Republic of China has not yet abandoned the Three Northeastern Provinces as its territory, and the National Government has not recognized "Manchukuo." Therefore, it should not be considered a friendly nation as mentioned in the decree on maintaining friendly relations. He hoped that the court would understand this. Subsequently, Mr. Cao Shoulian, the defendant's defense lawyer, spoke and further clarified this point. He also explained based on the facts that the elements of legal incitement did not exist. The judge, having heard both sides' statements, declared the debate concluded and scheduled the verdict for next Thursday.

Xinsheng News Agency reports: In order to reorganize its finances, the Hunan Provincial Government, through its Director of Finance He Haoruo, borrowed 1.4 million yuan from the Central Bank, the Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications. Ministry of Finance Approves That Purchase Orders from the General Chamber of Commerce Should Be Stamped

The Shanghai National General Chamber of Commerce received a reply from the Ministry of Finance, Tax Letter No. 10658, stating that the National General Chamber of Commerce's telegram dated June 9, 1936, requesting that purchase orders be exempt from stamp tax, has been noted. According to the regulations in Item 5 of the Stamp Tax Rate Table, which stipulates that receipts for goods and ledgers that are required to be stamped include all receipts, registered or unregistered, issued by shops of all kinds for the purpose of receiving goods. The remarks in the notes column, such as gift certificates, laundry tickets, and receipt books, are examples of the receipts in this item. Other receipts not listed but of the same nature should still be stamped according to the tax rate of this item. This is also clearly stipulated in Article 9 of the Implementing Rules. The receipt used by Shop A to collect goods from Shop B is used by Shop B for accounting and delivery of goods, which is the same as the case of using a receipt book to receive and deliver goods and record them. Therefore, it belongs to the nature of a receipt for goods and should be handled in accordance with the provisions of Item 5 of the tax rate table. Moreover, Article 5 of the Stamp Tax Law stipulates that tax stamps should be affixed to taxable documents before delivery or use. This purchase order becomes effective as a document when it is delivered to the other party, so it should be stamped before delivery. As for the case where the other party occasionally fails to deliver all the goods according to the order, it is another matter and does not invalidate the purchase order itself. If it is said that in this case, the purchase order is not effective and should not be stamped, then is there any reason to affix stamps after the fact if the goods are delivered according to the order? Previously, the Zhejiang Provincial General Chamber of Commerce and the Jiujiang Chamber of Commerce separately requested that these purchase orders be exempted from stamp tax, and they were rejected. Although the tax-exempt column in Item 5 of the tax rate table stipulates that "receipts under three yuan are exempt from stamping," Section 2 of Article 17 of the Stamp Tax Law stipulates that "if the amount is not specified, the tax stamp should be affixed at the highest tax rate of the type in principle." Therefore, if this purchase order does not specify the price of the goods, it should still be stamped with a two-cent tax stamp in accordance with the law. This is for your information.

General Federation of Trade Unions Convenes Various Labor Unions Yesterday; To Discuss Measures to Prevent Labor Unrest; Admonishes Workers Not to Strike or Go Slow Without Reason; And Appoints Representatives to Visit Director Pan of the Social Affairs Bureau to Discuss and Report

Ta Kung News Agency reports: In order to prevent labor unrest, implement labor-management coordination, and investigate illegal organizations formed under false pretenses, the Municipal Federation of Trade Unions convened a meeting of various labor unions at 2 PM yesterday. Several important cases were decided. The details are as follows:

Attending Representatives

Representatives from over eighty labor unions, including papermaking in the Fifth District, water and electricity in the Sixth District, soap and medicine in the Ninth District, cotton spinning in the Fifth District, shipbuilding in the Fourth District, medicine shops, military uniforms, dyeing, cosmetics in the First District, civilian boats in the Fourth District, papermaking in the First District, newspapers, cigarette making and winemaking in the Fourth District, civilian boat woodworking, tobacco, cleaning in the First District, elevator operators, dried ginger slices, taxi drivers, tea making in the Sixth District, hotels, medicine shops, papermaking in the First District, water and electricity in the First District, postal workers, postal employees, match making in the Fifth District, cigarette making in the Fifth District, porters, bleaching, rubber in the Fourth District, cotton spinning in the Second District, British-owned cars, cotton spinning in the Tenth District, tugboats, silk reeling in the Sixth District, silk reeling in the Fourth District, and shipbuilding woodworking, totaling over one hundred people, including Hu Menglin, Bao Boyang, Fang Rusheng, Zhang Dehua, Zhang Guanqin, Wang Jianchong, Liu Jintai, Zhao Zhenhui, Shen Jiabin, Shi Jikuan, Zhou Xuexiang, Li Mengnan, Ye Xianggao, and Wang Zhuping. Zhou Xuexiang was elected as the chairman and Fang Rusheng recorded the minutes.

Cases Decided

After performing the ceremony, the chairman first reported on the recent labor unrest situation and the General Federation of Trade Unions' assistance to the Party and government agencies in handling it, as well as the discovery of illegal organizations operating under false pretenses and disrupting the labor movement. Then, the discussion began. (A) How to prevent the frequent labor-management disputes in the city recently? Decision: (1) To issue a notice to all labor unions, admonishing their workers not to strike or go slow without reason and to implement labor-management coordination to promote production. (2) To advise employers in all industries not to suspend operations, reduce wages, or dismiss workers without reason. (3) To request the Party and government agencies to quickly resolve all labor-management disputes that have already occurred and are still under mediation in order to avoid conflicts. (4) To appoint Zhu Xuefan, Zhou Xuexiang, Lu Muqin, Ye Xianggao, Li Mengnan, Shui Xiangyun, Xi Yuting, Zhang Kechang, and Li Hua to visit Director Pan of the Social Affairs Bureau to request that all labor-management disputes be properly handled to avoid disagreements between the two sides and prevent renewed conflicts. (5) To request the Public Security Bureau not to arrest workers during the mediation period of labor-management disputes without the permission of the Party headquarters. (6) To request the government to allow representatives of the General Federation of Trade Unions to participate in the labor-management mediation committee. (B) Recently, an organization using the name "United Office of All Trades in Shanghai" has been distributing leaflets, wantonly disrupting the labor movement. How should this be handled? Decision: (1) To use the names of the various labor unions to jointly petition the central and municipal Party and government agencies to thoroughly investigate the instigators of the forged organization and severely punish them. (2) To request the Municipal Public Security Bureau to promptly interrogate the person who distributed the leaflets and has been apprehended, to reveal the instigator and punish them according to the law. Liu Jintai, Lu Muqin, Zhou Xuexiang, Li Mengnan, and Shui Xiangyun were appointed as five representatives to go to the Public Security Bureau to attend the hearing. Shui Xiangyun and Lu Muqin were appointed to draft the petition. The meeting adjourned at 5 PM.

Municipal Chamber of Commerce to Hold Design Committee Meeting Tomorrow

The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce notified all design committee members yesterday that the first design committee meeting of the current session would be held at 3 PM on the 12th of this month. A proposal from Chairman Xie Xiaochu was also printed and distributed, requesting that it be brought to the meeting for discussion. The proposals are as follows: (1) In the future, all companies and factories applying to the Social Affairs Bureau and Trademark Bureau for registration should be required to provide proof from the relevant trade association or chamber of commerce to ensure seriousness and avoid disputes. (2) For documents designated by the government that must be certified by the chamber of commerce to be eligible for passport application, certifications from other groups should not be accepted. (3) The certification of smuggled goods should be primarily handled by the relevant trade association or chamber of commerce. (4) Trade associations with similar business natures should be merged as soon as possible. (5) The Municipal Chamber of Commerce's membership fees should be thoroughly reviewed by the review committee to ensure fairness. Trade associations should also establish uniform regulations for the levels of membership and regular fees for members of the same industry. (6) The Municipal Chamber of Commerce should continue to strive for an increase in the number of executive and supervisory committee members.

The Shanghai Real Estate Association Held a Regular Meeting Yesterday to Discuss Ways to Save the Real Estate Industry. Pu Shen, Tian Xin, and Others Discussed the Continued Decline of the Real Estate Industry and Requested an Explanation of the Resale Mortgage Right as a Remedial Measure.

The Shanghai Real Estate Association held a regular committee meeting at its location on Shanxi Road yesterday afternoon. Shen Tianxin, Wang Yiting, Shen Lianfang, and others attended. Chairman Shen Tianxin discussed the issue of property debt disputes submitted by various Shanghai district courts for valuation, and exchanged opinions on the problem of saving the declining real estate industry. However, no decisions were made. The meeting adjourned at approximately 6 PM. A reporter from the Xinsheng News Agency interviewed Chairman Shen Tianxin yesterday. According to Mr. Shen, the Shanghai real estate industry is suffering from the impact of the overall economic downturn. Prices have plummeted, transactions have sharply decreased, and real estate merchants are on the verge of bankruptcy. Real estate is the largest asset in circulation in the market and is closely related to all industries. If we want to revive the market, we must first make real estate liquid. Although the government and other parties have been trying to find ways to remedy the situation, such as establishing a real estate mortgage bank, the real estate industry is still in decline. In areas such as Rue du Consulat and Beijing Road, which are known to be prosperous, empty houses are common and tenants are in arrears with rent. The courts are busy handling property debt disputes. This kind of economic downturn is difficult to resolve properly in a short time. This association has requested that the Ministry of Finance ask the Ministry of Justice to explain the resale mortgage right case, which is also one way to save the real estate industry. The Silver and Money Trades Association has also agreed with the principle. After consulting with the two associations, we will submit a request to the government for an explanation to remedy the situation.

### Wang Shubao, Owner of the Xiang Wu Stage, Was Accused of Murder. The Plaintiff Claims There Is Another Wang Shubao, but the Prosecutor Proves Private Reconciliation

Wang Shubao, the owner of the Xiang Wu Stage, was involved in a case during the January 28th Shanghai Incident where a dismissed detective, Ji Zhongtang, was shot and killed at the Xiangyan Bridge in Hongkou. This spring, someone distributed leaflets to various agencies, claiming that Wang Shubao was involved in a love triangle with the female performer Yu Yanfang, leading to the tragedy. Now, lawyer Huang Zongqia has reached a settlement with the family of the deceased and sought a dismissal of the case. Zhang Xiaowanzi (i.e., the plaintiff), a disciple of Ji Zhongtang, allegedly obtained a bribe and made false accusations. The former Chief Prosecutor of the Shanghai District Court, Zhong Shangbin, filed a lawsuit. Judge Wu Deying repeatedly summoned and questioned witnesses. However, the family of the deceased and witnesses all stated that the person who killed Ji Zhongtang was Wang Shubao from Anhui, not Wang Shubao from Yancheng, who was summoned. This raised the issue of two Wang Shubaos. The judge ordered an investigation, which has been ongoing for some time. Now, due to a change of judges, Yu Lüde is presiding over the case. Yesterday, Judge Yu reopened the trial. Wang Shubao testified that he is 48 years old and runs the Xiang Wu Stage. During the January 28th Shanghai Incident in 1932, the theater was used as a headquarters by Japanese soldiers. He moved to the concession to live. He did not know how Ji Zhongtang was killed in the war zone, nor was he involved with any female performer. After the war ended, he returned on May 29 and was arrested by the Public Security Bureau's detective team. Later, the plaintiff, Zhang Xiaowanzi, testified to the team that the Wang Shubao who committed the murder was a small gangster, another person. Therefore, Team Leader Lu Ying released him. He is now suffering an injustice. If this were true, he would be willing to be shot. Zhang Xiaowanzi testified that he is 30 years old, from Yancheng, and Ji Zhongtang was his mentor. On May 4, 1932, at 1 PM, his mentor was shot and killed by three people in a teahouse on Tianjin Road. One of them was named Wang Shubao, who had pockmarks and a northern accent. He reported the incident to the court himself. This is not that Wang Shubao. The family of the deceased and witnesses all claimed that this was not that Wang Shubao. The judge asked how much money they received for the reconciliation in the homicide case. They answered, "None." Yu Yanfang testified that she had no illicit relationship with Wang or Ji and was being slandered. Lawyer Huang Zongqia testified that he is 38 years old, from Yancheng, and accepted 60 yuan from Ji Chenshi in March of this year to file a lawsuit against Wang Shubao. He did not ask for any money for reconciliation. Prosecutor Tang argued that Wang Shubao had privately reconciled with Ji Chenshi for 1,100 yuan. The investigation confirmed this, so he requested a judgment. The judge adjourned the debate and said that the judgment would be announced later.

### Yellow Poisonous Moths Discovered Near Hongkou Park: The Moths' Yellow Powder Is Extremely Poisonous and Can Be Fatal

According to the Japanese Shanghai Daily News, a Japanese person was suffering from a severe poisoning at the Komaya Hospital in Yipin Lane, Wusong Road. On the evening of the 6th, a moth landed on his chest at his residence near Jiangwan Road. When he brushed it off with his hand, he suddenly felt intense pain and itching on his chest, abdomen, limbs, and back. He rushed to the hospital for treatment. According to the Komaya doctor's diagnosis, he was attacked by a highly poisonous moth. This poisonous moth is a small, yellow, scaly moth. When touched, it releases yellow powder, which is extremely poisonous and can be deadly. In the past, Japan suffered from this disease. In the Ganghwa Island and Haeju regions of Korea, there were more than 100 patients daily. Its toxicity is more intense than any poisonous insect. Even applying ammonia to the affected area cannot neutralize the poison. The most effective treatment is to use almond oil mixed with zinc oxide powder. Residents near Hongkou Park and Jiangwan Road are in a state of panic. Windows should be closed tightly before turning on the lights at night to prevent poisonous moths from flying in.

### Inside Story of the Suitcase Corpse Case Revealed: Two Victims Were Female Attendants at the Great World Amusement Park; Two Perpetrators Were Employees of the Fire Brigade; The Murder Was Planned After an Affair Was Exposed; Witness Lin Gendi Narrates the Scene

On the 11th of last month, a large green suitcase was discovered near the Waibaidu Bridge on Suzhou Road, containing the dismembered body of a woman without a head. Despite the police's best efforts to investigate, there were no leads until recently, when Huang Fusen, Liu Zhaonian, Chen Defu, Deng Shu, and other Chinese detectives from the Hongkou Police Station arrested a Ningbo woman named Lin Gendi, age 17, who lived at No. 32 Huacheng Lane, Xinjiang Road. She was a female attendant at the No. 22 booth at the Great World Amusement Park's Dajing Troupe. She was handed over to the First Special District Court and ordered to be detained. Following Lin's confession, Shao Yu, a driver from the Xinzha Fire Brigade No. 650 (father's name: Agou, age 27, resident of No. 74 Jinlu Lane, Parker Road), and Jiang Yuantan (also known as Xiao Fujian, Xiaotuzi), a firefighter from the Central Fire Brigade No. 231 (age 24, resident of No. 4 Dada Lane, Shikuta Road, Hongkou), were arrested yesterday morning. They were sent to Criminal Court No. 3 of the Special First Court and questioned by Judge Xiao Xiefei. Police lawyer Zhang Shizhu stated that since the suitcase corpse case occurred, the female suspect, Lin Gendi, was apprehended on the 23rd of this month. At the entrance of the Tongchangxiang Cigarette Paper Shop at No. 230 Carter Road, she loudly discussed how difficult it is for women to have affairs these days. If they are not careful, they may have their heads chopped off with an axe. Yu Hanwen, a shop assistant at the cigarette paper shop, and Du Changlin, the driver of trolleybus No. 148, overheard the conversation. Police detectives learned about it and arrested Lin. Under detailed questioning, Lin stated that the body in the suitcase was indeed Caiying, a female attendant at the Yang booth at the Great World Amusement Park. Initially, she was also a female attendant at the Great World, but later moved to the Shanghai Great World Amusement Park, so she knew Caiying. In May of this year, Lin met Shao Yu while making tea. On a certain day in June, Shao took Lin Gendi to Caiying's home in a rooming house at No. 3 Cunfu Lane, Baibao Road, North Sichuan Road. Jiang Yuantan was also present. There were no unusual activities that day. On August 8th, at 8 PM, Shao's father accompanied Lin to Caiying's home, and Jiang was also present. After a while, Jiang suddenly started arguing with Caiying, accusing her of having an affair with both him and Shao. Then Jiang started arguing with Shao. They discussed that such women were easy to find, but since this was the case, they might as well kill her. Jiang then pulled out an axe from his waist (because they were both wearing uniforms, they carried the axe with them) and chopped Caiying on the neck. Lin was terrified and ran away. One day later, on the 11th, Shao and others forced Lin to go to Caiying's home, saying that Caiying had been killed. When they arrived, Caiying's body was already in the suitcase, and her head was wrapped in a white cloth and placed in a bamboo basket, which was then covered with a straw bag. Jiang carried the straw bag, and Shao carried the suitcase out of the house. They hired three rickshaws to go to the Waibaidu Bridge. Shao threw the suitcase into the English Concession's wall. Jiang took the head out of the straw bag, added a stone, and threw it into the river, sinking it to the bottom. The police arrested Shao and Jiang and found a photo of a woman at Shao's home at No. 74 Jinlu Lane, Parker Road. Lin Gendi identified the woman in the photo as Caiying, who had been killed. The fingerprints on the photo and the fingerprints of the deceased were compared and found to be generally consistent. Yu Hanwen and Du Changlin have both arrived at the court today to testify. Lin Gendi's confession was recorded and submitted to the court. It was also stated that a more detailed investigation was needed, so it was requested that Shao and Jiang be detained. Yu Hanwen and Du Changlin testified that they did indeed hear Lin Gendi say that a girlfriend of hers had been killed with an axe. Lin Gendi was then brought from the detention center to the courtroom, and Shao and Jiang were questioned separately. Lin described the events in detail, which was the same as what Zhang Shizhu had stated (omitted). The judge then brought the two suspects to the dock and informed them that Lin had confessed to the events. Shao confessed that he met Lin Gendi through a firefighter from the Central Fire Brigade No. 434 in January. Lin insisted on marrying him and had repeatedly gone to his office, so he scolded her and kicked her out. Therefore, she is now framing him. He did not commit this crime. On August 8th, he was on duty and driving for the Western supervisor, so he had no time to go out. The photo that was found was a portrait of his wife, who is currently in Tongzhou. The judge did not believe him and could summon her for questioning. Wu Yuanying stated that he did not know Caiying at all and could not have killed her. He also did not know where Caiying's home was. The judge then ordered Lin Gendi to the stand to repeat what she had said and to identify the person in the photo. Lin repeated her statement and said that the photo was definitely of Caiying. However, Shao and Jiang firmly denied it, saying that they were being falsely accused and requested a thorough investigation. Judge Xiao reviewed the confessions and announced that the case would be postponed to next week for another hearing. Shao Yugen and Jiang Qianyuantan were remanded in custody.

### Pan Jingui and His Brother Sue for Fraud: Hu Zhichang Found Not Guilty; Hu Did Not Fight with the Pans; The Judge Has Learned the Truth

Hu Zhichang, the manager of the Great World Dance Hall at the intersection of Nanjing Road and Tibet Road, and Sun Ziming (i.e., Zhimin) were recently sued in the Criminal Court of the First Special Court by Pan Yugui and his brother Pan Jinmao, residents of No. 16 Songjia Lane, Beijing Road, who hired lawyers Ling Qihong and Huang Shaochang to accuse them of colluding to defraud them of money and inflicting injuries. Yesterday morning, Court President Qian Hongye presided over the joint trial in Criminal Court No. 1. Defendant Sun Ziming did not appear in court because his address was unknown and the summons could not be delivered. Only Hu Zhichang appeared in court with his defense lawyer, Xu Jia. Pan Jinfang stated that he and his older brother Pan Jingui used to work at the Huiling Deng Dance Hall. Later, Sun Ziming, who was from the same hometown, introduced them to Hu Zhichang. Hu, who was the manager of the Great World Dance Hall, was willing to let them run the cloakroom, toilet, and candy counter in the hall. He took a deposit of 450 yuan and a "activity fee" of 500 yuan. Tang Guanqing, a witness, saw 100 yuan of it being handed over. Unexpectedly, the two defendants saw that they were easy to deceive. They contracted the cloakroom to someone else and only offered them waiter positions. They pocketed the 500 yuan "activity fee." They repeatedly asked for it back but were refused. Later, they were not even given a waiter position. Therefore, on August 26th, at 3 PM, he and his brother went to ask for the money and retrieve the waiter's guarantee. They were beaten by Hu and he ordered dozens of gangsters to surround and beat them, causing serious injuries. Therefore, they filed a lawsuit, requesting that the defendants be punished according to the law and ordered to jointly return the 500 yuan "activity fee." Hu Zhichang testified that he did not know the two plaintiffs. Sun Ziming introduced them to contract the cosmetics display area of the dance hall. It was stated that the deposit was 500 yuan and the rent was 50 yuan. He paid 50 yuan in cash on July 25th and a check from the Silk Industry Bank on August 1st for 100 yuan. The remaining 400 yuan was to be paid before the opening. He also recommended the plaintiffs as waiters, and he agreed to hire them. Unexpectedly, when the check could not be cashed, he sent a letter to Sun Ziming urging him to pay, but he ignored it. He had no choice but to return the original check on the 12th and the 50 yuan in cash on the 24th, terminating the contract. He also returned the receipt he had issued to the plaintiffs, which can be verified in the accounts. Unexpectedly, on August 26th, the plaintiffs gathered four or five gangsters and came to cause trouble. They clashed with the guard, Zhao Haiqing, and went to the police station. He did not participate in the fight. He invited witnesses Zhao Haiqing and Tang Guanqing, the chief inspector of the Great World Amusement Park, to testify. After the lawyers for both parties debated, Judge Qian ruled in court that Hu Zhichang was not guilty and dismissed the plaintiff's attached civil suit. The trial of Sun Ziming was temporarily suspended.

### Shanghai Buddhist Association's Buddhist Movement

For the convenience of operations, the Shanghai Buddhist Association has moved to the Sanmei Temple in Xiaonanmen on September 6. The joint meeting of all directors and supervisors resolved to publicly recommend Master Dengxia to draft a plan consisting of six measures for publicizing the Buddhist movement: (1) Convene a general meeting of the association's members in the shortest possible time to participate in the Buddhist movement's publicity conference. (2) Send letters to various Buddhist organizations and social groups in Shanghai to arrange for members to go to these organizations to give lectures on the Buddhist movement to the extent possible. (3) Post slogans and pictures of the Buddhist movement in public places (such as train stations and docks), Buddhist organizations, along roads, and inside and outside the association's lecture hall. (4) Send members to public places, trains, ships, trams, and streets to distribute publicity pamphlets and leaflets on the Buddhist movement, and to give lectures on Buddhism. (5) Send letters to various theaters to arrange for them to screen the association's slogans and pictures of the Buddhist movement before each performance. (6) Send letters to various broadcasting stations to arrange for regular broadcasts or public lectures on Buddhism every week.

### Two Corpses Unearthed Due to Odor: Found Inside Women's Hospital

The house at No. 290 Tangshan Road, Hongkou, at the intersection of Zhaofeng Road, was originally church property and was previously used as a church. It is now leased by Renhe and used to open the Hongkou Women's Hospital, which is luxuriously decorated. Yesterday evening, a foul odor suddenly permeated the area, causing surprise and concern. People rushed to report it to the police at the post. The Huishan Police Station dispatched a large number of Chinese and foreign detectives, along with workers, in several cars to search the area. After arriving, they knocked on the door, but no one answered. They broke in through the window and opened the door, allowing the detectives to enter. They first searched the house but found nothing. They then opened the floor and were shocked to find two corpses, which had already decomposed. Their faces were blurred and unrecognizable. However, based on their clothing, it could be determined that there was a male and a female corpse. Detectives continued to search the scene, but the people from the hospital had already fled and disappeared. Whether this couple committed suicide or was murdered is unclear, but based on the circumstances, the latter seems more likely. The police are currently investigating the matter thoroughly.

On that day, they will sell corsages made by the nuns and the women housed at the home. The Good Sheperd's Home has been in Shanghai for two years, housing unemployed and impoverished women. They receive care and education at the home and are taught skills such as knitting, sewing, and washing so they can earn a legitimate income. Currently, the home is raising funds to build a laundry factory so that the women can work and support themselves. ### Indian Man Treats Child's Eye Disease, Child Suddenly Dies After Taking Medicine; Cause of Death Unknown After Examination; Stomach and Intestines Awaiting Testing

Xu Changming, a 37-year-old coolie from Jiangdu, who lives in a straw shed without a number on Feihong Road, Zhabei, has a son named Genbao, who is five years old. Recently, he suffered from a severe eye disease and had difficulty with bowel movements for a week. On the afternoon of the day before yesterday, Xu and his wife, Liu, took their son to the ophthalmology clinic of an Indian man named Gharam Singh (transliteration) at No. 623 Zhaofeng Road. The Indian man examined the child and asked for 15 yuan for medical expenses. Xu did not have that much money. After negotiations, the consultation fee was reduced to one yuan. Xu still could not raise the money, so he went home to get it. The Indian man gave the child medicine and laxatives to treat the disease. Unexpectedly, shortly after taking the medicine, the child suddenly died. When his father returned to the clinic and saw that the child was dead, he argued with the Indian man. Detective No. 2177 found out about it and reported it to the Huishan Police Station, which ordered detectives to investigate. They transported the child's body to the Shanghai Sanitarium for a brief examination, and then transferred it to the autopsy center on Ferren Road. Yesterday morning, Zhang Zongru, a prosecutor from the First Special District Court, along with forensic doctors Wei Ligong and Zhang Yan, and clerk Wang Zuyi, went to the center to examine the body. Xu Liu, the child's mother, stated that she said the Indian man often gave the child a mixture of red, green, black, and white liquids, as well as laxatives. Shortly after taking the medicine, the child died, so she requested justice. Gharam Singh, the Indian man, stated that he is 30 years old. He gave the child a laxative because he had difficulty with bowel movements. As for the liquid medicine, his mother gave it to the child herself. Zhang asked him if he had a medical license from the Municipal Council. He replied that he only sold Baoyan eye medicine, so he did not need a license. Zhang stated that the cause of death could not be determined from the appearance of the body. In order to clarify the truth, he ordered an autopsy. The autopsy report stated that the cause of death of the boy, Xu Genbao, was unknown and an autopsy was needed. After the autopsy, the body was handed over to his father, Xu Changming, for burial. A package of laxatives was given to the forensic doctor for testing. It is reported that forensic doctors Wei and Zhang have already performed the autopsy and have handed over the internal stomach and intestines to the Municipal Council's testing center for testing.

The Sorrowful Tale of Yang Xiuzhen: Driven to Despair by Poverty and Abandonment, She Attempts Suicide in a Hotel and is Rescued, Recounting Her Heartbreaking Ordeal

Yang Xiuzhen, a 33-year-old woman from Hangzhou, recently resided in room 23 of the Anle Hostel on North Zhejiang Road, using the name Wang Yangshi. On the 7th of this month, at 8:05 AM, she suddenly attempted suicide by consuming raw opium. A tea server discovered her and immediately reported it to the Huishi Police Station. Detective Shen Dehui rushed to investigate, while Yang was sent to the Sanatorium Hospital for treatment. Several suicide notes were found in the room, one of which detailed the suicide attempt. The content is worth recording, and here is an excerpt of the main points:

"I (referring to Yang herself), in the twelfth year of the Republic (1923), married Leng Fugen from Lvcheng, Danyang, through a matchmaker. We had a son named Yaoqing, now twelve years old. Our relationship was not bad, but Leng did not engage in proper work. In the eighteenth year of the Republic (1929), I encouraged him to come to Shanghai to find work, but he was unsuccessful. He happened to meet Wang Zhijing, a fellow villager of the owner of the Yunlaifu Button King store at 468 Fuzhou Road, who offered to introduce business and frequently lent money. However, his true intention was to seduce and possess a married woman from a good family. Later, he forced my husband to repay the debt. Unable to repay, my husband fled back to his hometown. Wang seized this opportunity and frequently harassed me. In a moment of weakness, I fell into his trap. From then on, I lived with him at 7 Weiyangfang, Baoshan Road. He gave my husband 100 yuan to divorce me. Afterward, I officially lived with him at [blank] Santuoli Lane, Baike Road. Later, I learned that Wang already had three wives and concubines, and I was forced to live as a minor concubine. Fearing abandonment, I had him sign an agreement. But in April of this year, Wang tricked me to a hotel on the road, got me drunk with wine, and when I woke up, Wang was gone. Later, when I went to Wang's place to ask for expenses, Wang said that I had signed a separation agreement in the hotel, so how could I come back to ask for money? Later, Wang even invited female hooligans to beat me severely. I then hired lawyer Shen Xing [blank] to sue him, but Wang wanted to reconcile. [Blank] As a result, there was no response. On May 10th, at about 11 PM, Wang ordered someone to tell me to go and negotiate a reconciliation. When I arrived at the entrance of the alley [blank], I was suddenly attacked with an axe by two people. The police arrested the assailants. The lawyer helped me book room 53 at the Anle Hotel, instructing me not to go out. After ten days, [blank] he asked me to pay the rent and go home (the following contains many accusations against the lawyer). I have repeatedly tried to assassinate Wang Zhijing to serve as a warning, but I have failed. In addition, due to financial difficulties, I am resorting to this fate," and so on. The suicide note also included a copy of the woman's complaint, filed on June 12th at the Civil Mediation Office of the First Special District Court, suing Wang Zhijing for neglecting his duty to provide alimony and requesting monthly payments of ten yuan in national currency, as well as a letter to her son, Leng Yaoqing. The handwriting is skilled, suggesting that she had received higher education, but there are many mistakes, which proves her state of mental distress at the time. It is now known that Yang has been rescued by the hospital's efforts and is out of danger. She will be discharged from the hospital soon."

Tong Rongsong, Convicted of Enticement, Appeals: Legal Arguments Examined, Hearing Concluded Yesterday, Judgment Scheduled

Tu Xiaoying, an 18-year-old woman from Ningbo, currently residing at 5 Yongxiangli, Datong Road, Zhabei, previously, through her uncle Tu Jianren and her mother Tu Chenshi as legal representatives, hired a lawyer to file a complaint in the First Special Court against Tong Rongsong (19 years old, residing at 6 Jinleli, Weihaiwei Road) from Tingdu for enticement and forgery. The first instance verdict found Tong Rongsong guilty of having illicit relations with a girl under sixteen, sentencing him to six months imprisonment, and two months for forgery, to be served consecutively as seven months. Prior to execution, he was to be sent to the Gongbuju Reformation Center for three months of moral education. It was permitted for bail of 5,000 yuan pending appeal. These details have been reported in this newspaper previously.

It is now known that Tong Rongsong, dissatisfied with the first instance verdict, hired lawyers Wu Linkun and Dong Chi to submit a written appeal to the Second Branch of the High Court, requesting that the original verdict be overturned and Tong Rongsong be declared not guilty. The appeal meticulously details the legal points, spanning several thousand words. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Yu, along with Assessors Zhou and Nie, convened a hearing. Both parties were questioned. Tong Rongsong admitted to having illicit relations with Tu Xiaoying, but claimed that the 2,000 yuan China Industrial Bank deposit book was written under duress and not of his own volition.

Subsequently, the appellant's lawyer, Wu Linkun, argued, "This case is divided into two points: facts and law. The facts were thoroughly investigated in the first instance and there are no major discrepancies, so we will not dwell on them. We will now focus on the legal points. The legal representative of the victim, Tu Xiaoying, in the original complaint was her uncle, Tu Jianren. This violates the litigation procedure. According to Article 212 of the Criminal Procedure Law, the legal representative or spouse of the victim may independently file a complaint. Also, the second paragraph states that if the victim has died, the complaint may be filed by the spouse, direct blood relatives, collateral blood relatives within the third degree, relatives by marriage within the second degree, or the head of the household. In this case, the victim, Tu Xiaoying, is not of age, but she is not deceased. According to the law, only her legal representative can file a private prosecution. Tu Jianren claims to be Xiaoying's uncle, and claims to be serving in the military and completely unaware [of the matter], hoping to avoid the statute of limitations. Her adoptive father and biological mother are both alive, but it is unclear on what basis he independently filed the private prosecution (the private prosecution was entirely initiated by Tu Jianren alone), which is difficult to understand. Furthermore, regarding the statute of limitations in Article 216 of the Criminal Procedure Law, the first instance record shows that Tong Rongsong and Tu Xiaoying had relations on May 6th of last year. When Tong paid 3,000 yuan, Tu Chenshi also knew that her daughter and Tong had a relationship. Therefore, Tu Chenshi was aware of the matter in May of last year. Article 216 of the Criminal Procedure Law stipulates that 'For crimes that are prosecuted only upon complaint, the complaint must be filed within six months from the time the person entitled to file the complaint becomes aware of the identity of the offender.' The statute of limitations has already expired. Moreover, Tu Xiaoying had indeed reached the age of sixteen when the relationship occurred. This is the reason for the appeal against the charge of illicit relations. Regarding the charge of forgery, although the passbook is printed with the words 'China Industrial Bank Savings Passbook', the page with the bank's seal and the manager's signature was torn off before the appellant wrote 2,000 yuan on it. It has lost its validity as a passbook and is obviously a discarded passbook. How can it be considered a document under criminal law? Therefore, we request that the original verdict be overturned and the appellant be declared not guilty. If the court deems it necessary to impose a sentence, we request that leniency be granted in consideration of the appellant's youth and ignorance, and that probation be granted."

Finally, the appellee's lawyer, Peng Qixiu, responded. After the arguments were concluded, the court announced that the judgment would be delivered on the afternoon of the 17th of this month.

Zhou Wei'shi, a wealthy merchant from Suzhou residing in Shanghai, had a physical relationship with a prostitute named Zhang Zhuying ten years ago, resulting in a son named Dunan. Impersonating Government Officials: Selling Official Positions for Profit in Shanghai, Mastermind Yu Dagong Flees, Three Accomplices Arrested

Yu Dagong has no legitimate occupation and makes a living by fraud. Recently, he conspired with Zhu Lingen from Changzhou, Wang Wenxi, Jin Ayu from Jiangyin, and others to impersonate the Second Division Command of the Jiangshan County Command Headquarters of Zhejiang Province. Under the pretext of recommending positions in the Jiangshan County Command Headquarters, they dispatched accomplices to defraud people of money and issued forged symbols and badges. The victims included Yang Pikang, Liu Yuesheng, Wang Guoliang, Tao Quanlin, Yang Baogen, and five others, who were defrauded of a total of 136 yuan. Together with Detective Shen Jinwen, they went to the Changzhou Hostel and arrested Zhu Lingen, Wang Wenxi, and Jin Ayu. However, the mastermind, Yu Dagong, had fled. They were taken to the police station, and [blank] magnetic badges, one cloth symbol, and four photos were found on each person. They were ordered to be detained. Yesterday morning, they were sent to the Ninth Criminal Division of the First Special Court. To gain the trust of the victims, they not only required them to pay registration fees and activity fees, but also had them take photos, as if the matter were real. The judge verified the confessions and ordered the three defendants to be detained pending a rescheduled hearing next Tuesday.

Establishment of a Tuberculosis Clinic to Promote Children's Tuberculosis Work: Adopting the Latest Children's Tuberculosis Rules and Laws, Low Fees Suitable for Long-Term Treatment

Since the Chinese Anti-Tuberculosis Association's Medical Committee and the Hongqiao Sanatorium organized X-ray group checkups, initially registered by the Shen Bao, the public has enthusiastically participated in the checkups, as they are related to the early diagnosis of lung disease. However, how to treat lung disease after it is detected has become a serious problem in terms of time and economy for those in the workplace and those with limited financial resources.

Dr. Ding Huikang, director of the Hongqiao Sanatorium in this city, recognizing this situation, has established a specialized "Tuberculosis Clinic" at No. A2, Daxilu, with the aim of serving the public with the latest scientific equipment and affordable fees. The clinic adopts the latest anti-tuberculosis rules and laws from various countries: (1) to popularize early diagnosis so that people do not delay medical treatment until their illness becomes severe, losing the proper time and opportunity for treatment; (2) to popularize physical therapy methods for treating lung disease, as the four major principles of lung therapy—sunlight, air, nutrition, and rest—are only supplementary therapies, and medicines, regardless of type, only have temporary or symptomatic effects and are of little value in fundamentally treating lung disease. Chinese people are superstitious about conditioning and do not know about isolation, leading to a rampant spread of the disease. To implement treatment, it is necessary to make the general public understand that in addition to all symptomatic and supplementary therapies, there are more reliable physical methods that can shorten treatment time, reduce the patient's suffering, save expenses, and increase social production and national construction capabilities; (3) to popularize sanatoriums; (4) to popularize health and insurance.

According to statistics in the United States, in 1904, there were 204 lung disease deaths per 100,000 people, which decreased to 67 in 1931. In recent years, the number of lung disease deaths has decreased even further. The reason for this is entirely due to the accurate proof of the pathological causes, the promotion of early anti-tuberculosis diagnosis, the progress of physical and surgical treatments, and the complete facilities of sanatoriums and public health. China must catch up urgently to promote anti-tuberculosis work.

The clinic has now hired Dr. Li Zubai, a medical doctor from the University of Berlin, Germany, and a former physician at the Internal Medicine Hospital of the University of Vienna, as the medical director. Consultation hours are from 9:00 AM to 11:00 AM and 5:00 PM to 7:00 PM daily, specifically to facilitate those in the workplace. The consultation fee is one yuan, and sputum tests are free. Long-term treatment, including X-rays, chemical tests, consultations, and various chemical and physical therapies, is very affordable. The location is No. A2, Daxilu, at the end of Fuxu Road. Dr. Ding's consultation hours for heart and lung problems are scheduled separately from 11:00 AM to 12:00 PM.

Pudong Waterworks Project Construction Expected to Be Completed by the End of the Year

According to the Outer Theory Agency's translation of the Continental News, the Pudong Waterworks Project is expected to be completed entirely by next spring, benefiting 120,000 residents. Currently, drinking water is mostly drawn from the riverbank or streams, with sediment mixed in the water, which is inconvenient and detrimental to hygiene. According to research by hygiene experts, Pudong is a center for the spread of infectious diseases. Fire and police authorities are also well aware that the inconvenience of obtaining water makes it difficult to control fires. Mayor Wu Tiecheng, when planning the construction of Greater Shanghai, had long foreseen this and made sure to address all aspects of development. Therefore, before proceeding with the construction of Pudong, he prioritized the laying of water pipes.

According to the construction plan, which was drafted in the winter of the previous year, the municipal government and the Greater Shanghai Waterworks Company requested its implementation. After inspection, it was found that many Pudong residents lived along the river. Therefore, the construction site was determined near the Youlong Road pier opposite Edward Road. The construction project is being undertaken by the Chengtai Construction Company at a cost of one million yuan. When completed, it will be one of the most modern waterworks projects in China. The machinery is being supplied by a German trading company in this city and can supply 350,000 gallons of drinking water per day. If future needs increase, it can be increased to 2.5 million gallons. Construction began a year ago. The water tower has been completed, and the internal water storage and sand filtration projects are under construction. In addition, the water plant office building is also under construction. It is hoped that all construction projects will be completed by the end of this year. The laying of water pipes is also progressing relentlessly, and it is said that one-third has been completed.

Although the waterworks is operated by the Greater Shanghai Waterworks Company, a commercial enterprise, the business plan focuses on public interests. Therefore, the water fees will be kept low. For users who cannot afford to install water pipes, water tanks will be set up at convenient locations on the streets for retail sales, with prices slightly lower than indoor installations to meet the general demand.

Due to its business needs, the Bureau requires a large quantity of general supplies, including printed materials and stationery. Dealing with stores for procurement at any time has become cumbersome. Although the procurement procedures are extremely meticulous, there is still concern about not demonstrating complete impartiality. To maximize openness, the Bureau will publicly invite bids for the following seven categories of major items: A. Printed materials, B. Stationery, C. Tea, D. Soap, E. Towels, F. Electrical supplies, G. Firewood, Toilet Paper, Western Toilet Paper and Brooms. Advertisements will be placed in newspapers for several days to invite merchants to bid. Lunch sets are available at 75 cents and one yuan and twenty cents, and dinner sets are available at one yuan and fifty cents, each with a complimentary bottle of Yantai beer and Yili soda. Such sacrifices can be described as an unprecedented initiative.

Letter

Dear Editor, I recently saw in your newspaper's September 9th issue of the "National Products" special section, that an article entitled "The first inventor of the water battery electrical lamp was the Hua Yi Industrial Company, which only produced a sample, and submitted it to the Ministry of Industry in June to apply for a patent, which was temporarily suspended due to insufficient capital and pending approval from the Ministry." After reading it, I was very surprised and alarmed. The water battery safety lamp invented by our company was approved for a patent by the Ministry of Industry. A notice was published in the Xin Shen and Shen Bao newspapers on August 11th and 12th. As for capital, it has been fully guaranteed. We are currently installing machinery and actively preparing for production to commence. The sections reported in the newspaper are obviously incorrect. Fearing that the outside world will not understand the truth and be confused by the rumors, we have sent this special letter to clarify and hope that you will correct it. Respectfully yours, the editor. Hua Yi Industrial Company of China, September 10th.

Weather Report

The Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday stated that Shandong is cloudy all around, but still clear and fine, with southwest to northwest winds. There are showers in the Yellow Sea. The Yellow River basin and the upper and middle reaches of the Yangtze River have light winds of uncertain direction. The lower reaches of the Yangtze River have fairly strong north to northeast winds. The typhoon in the East Sea, at 1:00 PM yesterday, had advanced to within 120 miles of 19 degrees north latitude and 128 degrees east longitude, hesitating to advance or proceeding very slowly. The wind force is unknown. Also, in the 24 hours before 3:00 PM yesterday, the temperature in this city reached a high of 77.0 and a low of 69.6. On the same day last year, the high was 95.7 and the low was 72.7.

Sports News

This Year's Western Football League Divided into Three Groups: A, B, and C, and Morning League. Group A Teams Must Join a Reserve Team and Set Up a Reserve Group. Davidson's Dual Management System Fails Again.

The Shanghai Western Football League's annual meeting was held at the Xitong Public School on Jiujiang Road at 5:15 PM yesterday. Eighteen representatives from various teams attended. Chairman Ge Linxu presided over the meeting and reported on the previous season's competitions and financial matters. Then, Litt announced the start of the election, and the reform plan of the league system was passed (as stated in the notice of the 17th of last month). However, Davidson's highly anticipated dual management system was rejected again by the league authorities and was not submitted to the general assembly for discussion, which is a strange thing. As for the teams, no proposals were put forward at this meeting. The meeting adjourned at about 6:00 PM. The details are as follows:

Participating Teams

The deadline for registration for this year was the 5th of this month. As a result, a total of forty teams were obtained. Subsequently, the Public School of the Public Concession requested to join, and it has also been approved. Therefore, the total number reaches forty-one teams. The Youyou team will continue to join this year. The Jinan team has also registered to join this year. The lineup of both sides is currently unknown, but most of Youyou's main players last year were Jinan athletes. Now that Jinan has been reorganized, its main players will naturally return to their parent team. Therefore, the strength of Youyou this year will be noted by the general public. Also, this year's Donghua Stadium will be the main venue for the Municipal Sports Stadium. In the future, various competitions in the league may be held at the Municipal Sports Stadium. As for the forty-one teams participating in this session, there are a total of six new members, and the other thirty-five teams are old members. The detailed allocation will be reviewed and implemented by the executive committee of the association and then announced. The full list is as follows:

List of Teams

French Business, Youyou, Donghua, British Army, Lux, Portugal, Western Business, Western Police, Jewish, Shell, St. Francis, British Navy, St. John's, Aurora, Hygiene, French Army, Qinghua, Russian Army, Surveying, Chinese Police, Elementary, Seville, Apperon, Tongwen, Public Union, Guanglu, Railway, Asia, Vitesse, Yousheng, Russian Overseas Chinese, Lansd, Calsa, Pader, Fire Brigade, Jinan, Dongguang, Nie Zhongcheng, Jinde, Bank of Communications, Public School of the Public Concession.

Election Results

The association's annual election has always adopted a voting method. This year, it was changed to an election by nomination. Moreover, each representative received a pre-determined list printed on a typewriter. As a result, the list was passed without any objections. The chairman remains Mr. Ge Linxu. There are four vice-chairmen. Except for Kueil, who was replaced by Ma Qi, there were no other changes. In addition to the five chairman and vice-chairmen who are ex officio members, four people were elected by the general assembly yesterday, and only one new member, Kang Bosi, was added. In addition, five members of the new chapter drafting committee were elected to be responsible for drafting the new constitution and new rules. The list is as follows:

Chairman Ge Linxu, Vice-Chairmen Bo Lieqi, Litt, Ma Qi, Shen Siliang, Executive Committee Members Ma Xuer, Kang Bosi, Lei Yanshi, Ke Huat, New Chapter Drafting Committee Ma Qi, Ke Huat, Ai Qixun, Ga Xu, Huo Hua.

Shen's Speech

Then Mr. Shen Siliang was invited to give a speech, which mainly stated that "Although a Chinese football team failed to win the victory in the World Games, it has received an honor, that is, the technology of the Chinese team has been praised by various countries in the world. The Shanghai Football League has been in a very important position in the country, and the future is immeasurable. I hope that the feelings of each team will become more profound, so that Shanghai's football industry can reach the world."

Principles of Reorganization

The association passed the reform plan of the league system for this year, which was planned by the executive committee of the association, on the 17th of last month. Yesterday, it was submitted to the annual meeting for discussion by the member teams. Ge Linxu read it item by item and explained everything. From the first to the eighth items, all were passed without objection. Only the "or" in the seventh item was changed to "and." In the ninth item, Ai Qixun and the representative of the Western Police team spoke successively. As a result, it was revised to increase the number of members of the League Committee to six (originally five), with one elected by the Group A teams, one by the Group B teams, and one by the Group C teams. This plan is still a principle, and the trial period is two years, until 1938. Yesterday, five members of the new chapter drafting committee were elected to be responsible for drafting the new constitution and new rules. The reformed principles passed yesterday are recorded below.

New Charter Contents

(1) This year's Shanghai Western Football League is divided into three groups (Groups A, B, and C).

(2) Set up a "Reserve" group, which is specifically for the reserve teams of Group A to join the competition. Players can also participate in Group A competitions without restrictions. Additional prizes will be awarded.

(3) Member teams joining Group A must join a reserve team in the Reserve Group.

(4) The bottom team in Group A must be demoted to Group B, and the champion of Group B can be promoted to Group A (but must join a reserve team in the Reserve Group). The bottom team in Group B is demoted to Group C, and the champion of Group C can be promoted to Group B.

(5) Another (Sunday Morning League) is established, which is the successor to last year's Group E, with a limit of ten teams.

(6) All member teams can join the League or the "Sunday Morning League."

(7) All member teams can join the League or the Sunday Morning League.

(8) The winner of each game gets two points, the loser gets zero points, and a draw gets one point each. If the score is the same after the end, the average score is calculated.

(9) The number of members of the League Committee for this season is six, three of whom are selected from the executive committee, and the remaining three are selected from the member teams, one is elected by the Group A teams, one is elected by the Group B teams, and one is elected by the Group C teams. Each team is only allowed to put forward one representative to participate in this election. This committee has no power to interfere with administration, but must report to the executive committee for processing.

According to Mr. Speake, Davidson's "dual management system" is a novel and perfect plan based on the latest British football rules, but since the powers are divided, management will be difficult, so the association did not adopt it, which is a pity.

News from the Municipal Guoshu Hall: Holding a Member Graduation Examination

The Shanghai Municipal Guoshu Hall has been established for eight years. A member graduation examination is held once a year. Members who have practiced for the specified number of years can participate in the examination. Those who pass the examination will be issued graduation certificates of various levels by the hall. This year's member graduation examination is divided into three levels: advanced, intermediate, and elementary, and is scheduled to be held on September 13th at the fifth training ground of the Tianhou Palace. An examination committee has been organized to be responsible for examination and selection. It is also learned that the hall is currently seeking half-year members. Those who are interested in practicing guoshu can go to the general hall at Xinkaihe, Minquan Road, and the special district office of the Tianhou Palace to request a brochure and register.
