Our Country's World Games Football Team Wins Against Geneva Servette: Geneva Newspapers Unanimously Praise

Central News Agency Geneva Dispatch: For several days, large advertisements have been hung on the streets and alleys of Geneva, stating, "The Geneva Servette team is scheduled to have a friendly match with the World Games Chinese football team at 6:15 pm on the 20th of this month." It goes without saying how eagerly those in Geneva who are interested in sports are awaiting this day. Even those who usually do not pay much attention to sports are rubbing their fists and preparing to watch. Rather than saying they are watching the game, it would be better to say they are curious, because this is an unprecedented event in the Geneva sports world: the first contact with the young men of the Central Plains. What kind of skills do Chinese athletes possess? This is what they are eager to experience. Most people here base their predictions of victory or defeat on physique and skill, as if the Servette team holds a sure winning ticket. The Servette team, having experienced many formidable opponents, seems not to take the Central Plains athletes to heart. Moreover, the psychology of the masses is enough to increase their arrogance. However, the Geneva newspapers are already cautious about them. Three days before the match, the attitude of the newspapers seemed to be giving them some warnings. The Geneva newspaper (Journal'de Geneve) on the 18th of this month stated, "The Servette team will play against the Chinese football team on the evening of the 20th. We should know that these eleven chosen players of the Celestial Dynasty (referring to the Chinese team) have secured victory in twenty-three out of twenty-nine international matches in the past. Four times, the strength was evenly matched. Although they lost to England once in the World Games, it was a glorious defeat... Therefore, requests for matches continue to pour in..." It went on to say, "The Chinese team is very strong in terms of technique, and their speed of movement is unpredictable..." The same day, the Swiss Daily (Lasuisse) said, "This is a unique opportunity, because the Chinese team is on a traveling tour and will definitely arouse special interest among the audience... And this match will probably not be ordinary, because the team (China) has competed against the strongest Germany..." On the 19th, the Geneva Tribune (La Tribune de Geneve) said, "...The Servette club never disappoints their audience, because they only invite the most famous football teams of the moment to their field. Tomorrow evening, they will meet the players of the Chinese World Games team. How excited and anxious the audience is to wait... For a long time, this is the first time a famous friendly army has been invited..." It can be seen that in their proud anticipation, they also expressed doubts. On the evening of the 19th, many overseas Chinese were waiting on the platform of the Geneva train station. In addition, there were representatives of the Servette club. Everyone's eyes seemed to be focused in one direction. In the sound of the turning wheels, the twenty-two Central Plains athletes arrived in Geneva and stayed that night at the hotel booked by the Servette club. Reporters also went to the hotel to talk briefly with the Chinese team members. At that time, observing their tired expressions from the journey, they were quite worried about the match tomorrow. Overseas Chinese who met at the hotel had the same feeling without prior agreement. Because they were the host and we were the guest, they were relaxed and we were tired. Although we had words of encouragement, we did not dare to be too optimistic in our hearts. After returning to our accommodation, we could hardly sleep.

The next day (the 20th), as the time of the match approached, the reporter went to the hotel at 4:30 to have tea with the team members. At 5:30, they set off together. Seeing that everyone's fatigue from the journey had not recovered, their spirits were invigorated, and they were happy and harmonious. They chatted and laughed in the car, feeling relaxed and content. The strangest thing was that no one mentioned the match, as if they did not care about winning or losing. It cannot be said that they were not used to formidable opponents and had seen it all before. The reporter also gained a lot of courage because of this.

The Servette field is far in the suburbs. After a fifteen-minute drive, we arrived. However, the national flag of the Republic of China, with the blue sky, white sun, and red earth, and the Swiss flag, fluttering in the wind on the high poles extending out of the field, had already caught our eyes. The reporter then said to the Chinese team members, "This is the first time, the first time our national flag has flown over a Swiss football field. We hope it will fly many more times." The team members smiled at each other.

When we first arrived, there were not many spectators, but when the opening ceremony began, the four sides were already surrounded by crowds. The front box seats were already feeling overwhelmed, so they had to temporarily raise the price. There were more than 3,000 spectators. It's a pity it wasn't a Saturday afternoon or Sunday, otherwise the audience would have been several times larger.

The match began. The Servette representative presented the Chinese captain with a bouquet of flowers to express a friendly welcome, which was very courteous. In the first twenty minutes, Servette's attack was extremely fierce, and our side seemed to focus on defense and failed to counterattack. At this time, the reporter turned to look at the audience, and some overseas Chinese were pale, and some were anxious and uneasy, not knowing how worried they were. But in an instant, the first goal was kicked into the opponent's goal by Mr. Li Huitang. Our side turned from defense to attack, and the enemy's formation showed chaos. However, the other side had a better physique, with long legs and tall bodies, which gave them a lot of advantage, so at the end of the first half, the score was tied at two to two. But a few times when our side's attack was tense, the other side kicked the ball back into their own camp or out of the field to avoid danger, which was a bit too unsportsmanlike, so the audience booed in unison to express their dissatisfaction. And when our side won, the audience also applauded equally without bias. The fair attitude of the audience caused the other side's goalkeeper to scold, "Stupid audience..." This was certainly very rude, but when I think back to my attitude at the time, I couldn't help but be too biased, because I only applauded for my own side. But I believe the overseas Chinese were just like me.

In the first half, our side's formation was as follows:

Huang Jiliang

Li Tiansheng, Mai Shaohan

Chen Zhenhe, Xu Yahui, Zhang Xianyuan

Zhuo Shijin, Sun Jinshun, Li Huitang, Feng Jingxiang, Yang Shuiyi

Reserves: Cai Wenli, Huang Meishun, Li Guowei, Cao Guicheng, Jia Youliang. In the second half, our side's formation was slightly changed, that is, Jia Youliang replaced Yang Shuiyi, and Yang Shuiyi replaced Zhuo Shijin. The second half started ten minutes later. Because the outcome had to be decided within forty minutes, both sides became more energetic, and the audience was even more nervous. In this half, both sides were penalized. Most of our side's penalties were due to touching the ball with their hands. In addition, our side was the most disciplined, which won the sympathy of the audience. In the first twenty minutes, our side scored another goal. In the next twenty minutes, the two sides fought even harder. The other side tried to restore the balance, but failed. In the end, our side won by three to two. The overseas Chinese's anxious mood half an hour earlier had turned into high spirits, as if they had won the supreme honor. The audience also applauded continuously, and many people came to congratulate our team members. Many children surrounded our team members, patting their shoulders and shaking their hands, expressing their admiration and respect in an innocent and innocent way. At nine o'clock that evening, our delegation to the League of Nations and the delegation to the International Labour Organization jointly hosted a banquet for the team members at the Geneva Chinese Restaurant to wash away the dust and celebrate the victory. The guests and hosts were all happy and did not disperse until nearly midnight. The Chinese team went to Paris the next morning. It is said that they will play two matches in Paris, one in Harvard, and two in London. They are scheduled to return to China by ship from Naples, Italy, on the 4th of the month.

The next day, the Geneva newspaper (Journal de Geneve) began with the sentence, "What a surprise! Servette was defeated by the Chinese World Games team." The audience was driven by curiosity or wanted to see the skills of the Chinese team members who had fought against England for eighty minutes at the World Games fifteen days ago. On the other hand, because the Japanese World Games football team played against the Grashoppers team (editor's note: on the evening of the 10th, the Japanese World Games football team lost to the Grashoppers by zero to sixteen), they did not believe that the Chinese team was a strong opponent of Servette. But as a result, we believed that Chinese football was better than Japanese football. In the section describing the match, the newspaper said that Servette did show great effort at the beginning of the match. The Chinese defense was often under their pressure. The Chinese side seemed only able to parry and unable to counterattack, but the agility of the Chinese defenders and the power of the forwards were unexpected. In the blink of an eye, they turned from defense to attack. It went on to say that the Chinese team members had a solid belief in their forwards (referring to Li Huitang), so their spirits were very consistent, and their passing speed was unpredictable. At the same time, their main player (Li Huitang) never let them down. Finally, it said... In terms of physique and technique, Servette should have had the advantage. If the Chinese team can put more effort into technique, even the famous European teams will have to be shaken. The newspaper also encouraged Servette to learn from their strengths and make efforts to reorganize. The same day, the Swiss Daily said, "We were very curious to wait for the friendly match between Servette and China. Servette had played many matches with famous European teams and even African teams, but this was the first time they had played with an Asian team. This time, China won. However, Servette's fierce attack in the first half forced the Chinese team to only parry and unable to fight back. People generally thought that China's match against Servette would be like Japan's match against the Grashoppers team. At the very least, Servette could defeat the Central Plains players by four or five to zero. In the end, they did not expect that their goalkeeper's agility was enough to defend, and the forward's ferocity was able to kick the ball in from a distance of 25 meters. The speed of their team members' passing was truly without loss. In contrast, we felt that the Servette players' movements were too slow." The newspaper also said that in terms of technique, Servette should not have lost, but at that time, Servette's formation was chaotic, and their attitude was sometimes unsatisfactory. The forward protagonist and the Chinese team's strong players were even more unmatched.

Indeed, the Chinese team's expedition, on a tiring journey, with 29 international matches, was able to win 23 times and draw 4 times, which cannot be said to be surprising. At the same time, it also broke the Europeans and Americans' long-standing perception of our country's sports world. This immortal memorial is indeed one of the best ways to promote our country. Out of love and admiration, we sincerely hope that our team members will take the experience of this expedition, learn from their strengths, and make further progress. In the future, their importance in the international arena can be asserted.

The reporter still remembers that in July of this year, Professor Zhang Pengchun of Nankai University passed through Geneva and gave a five-day academic lecture at the Geneva Institute of International Studies. The audience increased gradually, and each lecture was met with thunderous applause for several minutes. Almost all the professors of the University of Geneva were mobilized, and its impact was unprecedented. Within a month, the Chinese sports world won another victory here. How fortunate and honored it is for the overseas Chinese in Geneva to participate in this joyous event.

Education News

Peking Research Institute's Seventh Anniversary: Li Shuhua Reports on Research Work and Funding: Rubbing Exhibition and Academic Lectures in Huai Ren Hall

(Special Dispatch from Peking) The National Peking Research Institute held its seventh anniversary celebration today (the 9th) at 9:00 am in the auditorium of the institute inside Yunliao Gate. The director of the institute, Li Shihui, was unable to return to Peking due to matters in Nanjing. Deputy Director Li Shuhua presided over everything. The academic community of Peking was extremely enthusiastic in attending. Those who attended included Xu Bingchang, Wu Zhengzhi, Tao Xisheng, Li Linyu, Fook Kenson, Li Shutian, Cha Liangzhao, and representatives from all walks of life, totaling about 200 people. When the meeting began, etiquette was observed. First, Chairman Li Shuhua reported on the overview of the seven years of work. Then, Xu Bingchang, director of the Historical and Archaeological Group of the institute, reported on the joint rubbing exhibition organized by the institute and the National Peking Library. The details are recorded as follows:

Li Shuhua's Report

Today is the seventh anniversary of the institute. The director originally planned to attend, but he could not return to Peking due to matters in the south. He expressed his extreme apologies. The institute began preparations in 1928 and was formally established in 1929. It has now been seven years. The guidelines set at the time of establishment were to cooperate with various agencies and academic groups. Over the years, there have been many cooperative projects with various parties. The Radium Research Institute and the Pharmaceutical Research Institute cooperated with the Sino-French University. The Geological Research Institute cooperated with the Industrial Geological Survey. The institute cooperated with the Academia Sinica and various universities to organize the Pacific Science Association and establish marine biological research institutions. The Bohai Marine Biological Research Laboratory was established in Yantai, and specialists were sent to Yantai to collect and conduct research. It also cooperated with the Qingdao Municipal Government to form the Jiaozhou Bay Marine Animal Collection Group. Regarding archaeological work, the institute cooperated with the Shaanxi Provincial Government to form the Archaeological Society to carry out surveys of historical sites and excavations of antiquities in Shaanxi. The institute's regular expenses are 30,000 yuan per month. We ourselves feel that we have not dared to waste the 30,000 yuan per month for the country, which is still not sufficient. Fortunately, the various Boxer Indemnity agencies have helped a lot. The Sino-French Boxer Indemnity subsidized the Radium Research Institute with 7,000 yuan, the Pharmaceutical Research Institute with 7,000 yuan, and 20,000 French francs. The Sino-British Boxer Indemnity subsidized equipment costs with 100,000 yuan and subsidized the Physics Research Institute with 60,000 yuan and the Chemistry Research Institute with 40,000 yuan. We are deeply grateful for the subsidies from the various Boxer Indemnity funds.

Xu Bingchang's Lecture

Taking advantage of the Peking Research Institute's seventh anniversary celebration, various rubbings are displayed in Huai Ren Hall. These items were all collected during archaeological excavations in Shaanxi. Among them, many are important parts. Today, the rubbings are displayed, but they are all displayed in groups. The most precious ones are the stone statue of Emperor Taizong of Tang and the Laozi's Tao Te Ching. The origin of Chinese stone carvings, such as stone drums and stone carvings, is the oldest, while stone statues seem to have been created in the time of Emperor Wu of Han, more than 2,000 years ago. The stone carvings of Zhang Qian, Marquis Wu of Wang, and Kunming Pool are also very famous at one time. A lot of Han paintings were discovered in Puyang. The exhibits are mostly items that have not been seen outside. The stele of Laozi's Tao Te Ching was discovered in Shaanxi and is octagonal in shape. Very few remain.

Wu Zhengzhi's Lecture

In summary, while Peking Research Institute celebrates its seventh anniversary today, the Chinese scientific community has also made great progress in these seven years. Although science started early and research was initiated, the fields of physics and chemistry have made significant progress compared to thirty years ago. The achievements can be seen everywhere. Peking Research Institute has also made the greatest contribution in the seven-year process. Peking is the cultural center of the country, and the famous scenic spots and buildings can all express the great spirit of China. It is fortunate that the research institute can exist in this cultural area, and it is also fortunate that the cultural area has this emerging scientific organization.

Tao Xisheng's Lecture

The topic was the relationship between academia and society. The general idea was that in the past seven years, not only has academia made progress, but society has also made progress, because the progress of society has influenced the progress of academia. The progress of society in recent years has been caused by the collapse of the social economy. The past seven years in China can be said to be the most unfortunate period, with disasters, banditry, and so on. But these various adverse phenomena have their future hope. As for scientific products, if society cannot accept them, they will never be able to promote social progress. The old mentality and the new organization are difficult to match. The old mentality is entirely based on the aspect of profit. For example, the spinning wheel of small handicrafts, if driven by a motor, will certainly not be able to cope. In other words, it should be considered whether society has the ability to accept science. To seek social and scientific progress, the old organization of Chinese society has completely collapsed, and there is an urgent need for new science. It is hoped that the colleagues of the research institute will pay attention to how to apply the results of their research to society in the future. After the lecture,

Lunch

The meeting did not begin to disperse until 2:00 pm. After the meeting, a photograph was taken in the empty space of Fuchang Hall behind Huai Ren Hall to mark the occasion. Then, they went to Huai Ren Hall for lunch, with about 100 people. There was a lot of talk and laughter during the meal, which was quite lively. It did not disperse until about 1:00 pm. (Anonymous) September 9th

The Recent Four Years (V) of National Central University

— Luo Jialun

(3) Reorganizing Student Dormitories

In the past, most of the student dormitories of our university were rented from private houses, resulting in them being scattered in various locations, which was extremely inconvenient for management. Furthermore, non-university students often mixed in to stay, which not only violated school rules but also increased school expenses and disrupted public order. In view of this, our university believed that reorganizing the dormitories was a matter of utmost urgency. Therefore, despite extremely difficult economic conditions, we managed to raise a large sum of money to build two relatively large dormitories, and returned all the previously leased houses. This allowed a portion of students to be concentrated in the first dormitory on campus, female students to be concentrated in the female dormitory on campus, and the majority to be concentrated in the newly built dormitory. All students were assigned rooms by person, so that the school could easily manage them and students could easily study on their own. After this reorganization, not only was management more convenient, but the dormitories took on a neat and orderly appearance. Moreover, the problem of non-university students residing in dormitories, which had been criticized by society and neglected by the government for many years, was completely resolved.

9. Expanding the Area of University Property

Over the past four years, there has also been a significant increase in the area of university property. With the kindness of the Jiangsu Provincial Government, it was decided to allocate the Wulong and Mufu Mountains near the suburbs to our university. The Wulong Mountain area is more than 7,700 mu, and the Mufu Mountain area is more than 6,000 mu, totaling more than 13,700 mu. In addition, farmland was purchased and expanded in Kunshan and Jiangpu counties, totaling 118 mu. Furthermore, a sixth dormitory for faculty and staff was purchased near the main campus, costing 11,804 yuan (this was purchased at the end of the 21st year, before the decision to build a new campus site). (Recently, more than 5,000 mu of land was purchased for the new campus site at market price.) This is a general overview of the increase in university property.

10. Centralizing the Location of Colleges to Facilitate Observation and Learning

Previously, the locations for offices, classes, and research of various colleges were extremely scattered. Some departments of the same college were in different locations, and even within a single department, different courses were taught and experimented in different places. After several planning sessions, they are now more centralized. Currently, Zhongshan Yuan is used as the College of Liberal Arts, the Science Hall as the main building of the College of Science, Southeast Yuan as the College of Law, Nan Gao Yuan as the main building of the College of Education, and the New Classroom as the main building of the College of Engineering. The College of Agriculture has always been concentrated in Sanpailou and has not been changed.

11. Centralizing Administrative Agencies to Increase Office Efficiency

Previously, the office locations of various administrative departments and groups were extremely scattered, making communication inconvenient and supervision difficult. Now, the two wings of the auditorium have been re-partitioned and properly arranged, and all of the school's administrative agencies have been moved in. This saves time and naturally increases efficiency.

12. Reforming the Accounting System

The supervision and assessment of the school's finances depends on the accounting system. Due to long-standing habits, the school's accounting was disorganized and lacked established procedures. This led to abuses, even allowing people to sell or buy public property on behalf of others without any restrictions. Therefore, three accountants were hired to establish a proper accounting system, which was promulgated and implemented in the autumn of the 21st year. This was even before the government formulated accounting regulations. The aim was to ensure that all accounts were clearly categorized and readily available for inspection and submission at any time. In addition, the procedures for general affairs were clarified, standard prices were made public, and samples of items were retained for regular audits.

13. Maintaining Regular Payroll to Ensure the Stability of Faculty and Staff Life

For the past four years, thanks to the government's support, educational funding has not been deficient. However, during the crises of the Rehe Incident and the Fujian Incident, our university repeatedly experienced financial difficulties. But no matter what, we have always maintained the prescribed payroll period and have never delayed it by even a day, in order to maintain the stability of the lives of faculty and staff.

14. Reorganizing Debts

The school's old debts were deeply accumulated, some dating back to the Southeast University era. During this period, efforts were made to reorganize them, and a committee was organized to review the documents. A total of 97,899 yuan and 22 cents were repaid successively. Those that could not be handled were deferred. However, during my tenure, all purchases were made according to the policy of "preparing before purchasing," so there were never any arrears. Our international credit has gradually been restored.

15. Establishing Scholarships and Publicly Funded/Free Student Places

In order to encourage student scholarship and help poor students, starting from the 21st academic year, seventy scholarships were set up each semester, totaling 140 scholarships per year, each worth fifty yuan per semester. A committee organized by professors publicly assessed and awarded scholarships to students with excellent academic performance. Starting from the 25th academic year, in accordance with the Ministry's order, the scholarship system was abolished and replaced with publicly funded/free student places. The number of publicly funded students was set at 20 to 28, and the number of free students was set at 50 to 70.

16. Raising Admission Standards and Paying Attention to School Examinations

University education should emphasize quality over quantity, and it must be so in order to raise standards and develop academics. Therefore, from the 22nd academic year to the present, professors have been hired as examination committee members for each entrance examination to handle the examinations seriously and eliminate all forms of solicitation and malpractice, so that the students' levels are more uniform. However, the number of freshmen in each session has been increasing year by year. As for the various examinations in the school, in addition to the graduation examination, a committee is organized separately in accordance with the Ministry's order, and scholars from inside and outside the school are hired to preside over it together. All other examinations are handled seriously by the professors. Regular examinations, such as required courses such as English and Mathematics, all use the cumulative system to ensure strictness. Therefore, general coursework is becoming more and more serious. (To be continued)

Annual Meeting of the China Vocational Education Society - Members Return to Shanghai - Reportedly, the Spirit of the Meeting Was Excellent - All Proposals Were Practical

The 16th Annual Meeting of the China Vocational Education Society and the 14th National Vocational Education Discussion Conference were held in Chengdu, Sichuan Province, starting on the 16th of this month. The meeting has ended. Shanghai members such as Jiang Wenyu, Yang Weiyu, He Qingru, Yao Huiquan, and Jia Foru, after the meeting, assisted the Sichuan provincial authorities in planning vocational education and stayed for many days. Now that their work is finished, they have returned to Shanghai by taking the Minsheng Industrial Company's ship. According to them, more than 200 members registered for this annual meeting and vocational education discussion conference. The spirit was excellent, and all proposals were practical.

To the Young Women

— Dr. Chen Xingfen, Female Physician, Head of Gynecology at Hongkou Maternity Hospital

A woman's health and beauty is, as everyone knows, indicated by her menstruation. If menstruation comes normally and recurs regularly, it generally indicates that her sexual function is not showing any abnormality, and it also suggests that her body is not undergoing any significant changes. Naturally, she is healthy and lively.

Normal menstruation indicates the soundness of a woman's body. Irregular menstruation indicates a woman's physical weakness. Therefore, menstruation serves as a measure of a woman's physical health. I often see young women with pale complexions, depressed spirits, and weakened bodies, and after examination and inquiry, nine out of ten cases are due to abnormalities in their menstruation.

The symptoms caused by menstrual irregularities are generally pain before and after menstruation. The menstrual flow is either excessive or insufficient. The menstrual cycle is irregular, occurring several times a month or once every few months. The lower abdomen and waist often feel distended and painful. Blood and energy are deficient, leading to various symptoms of neurasthenia, such as headaches, insomnia, stiff shoulders, palpitations, poor appetite, nausea, constipation, frequent urination, dizziness, fatigue, edema, general lassitude, dysfunction of the reproductive organs, pain during intercourse, decreased libido, frigidity, and lack of sensation. The various conditions of these symptoms, as described by the patients themselves, are quite numerous.

The miserable state of young women suffering from menstrual problems is truly indescribable. It ruins the beautiful dreams of couples and causes discord in the family. Because of the mental anguish, the happiness of youthful health and beauty is completely eroded by this menstrual pain. How regrettable! Therefore, menstrual disorders must be treated appropriately as early as possible, and attention must be paid to health maintenance. It must not be underestimated or ignored.

Among the medications for treating menstrual irregularities at home, 'Menorrin' is indeed effective in clinical practice. This medicine is effective for gynecological diseases such as menstrual irregularities and leucorrhea, as well as hysteria (i.e., neurasthenia in women). Taking 'Menorrin' can promote the development of female sexual organs, regulate menstruation, satisfy sexual desire, promote metabolism, remove blood stasis and generate new blood, replenish blood and strengthen the body, and prevent aging in women. For those who have been married for a long time without conceiving, using it to regulate menstruation and promote fertility is invariably effective. Numerous doctors have confirmed its effectiveness, considering it to be the source of women's health.

Commercial News

Finance: Pure Gold Plummets to .203 — Market Conditions Return to Slackness —

The gold market saw a sharp drop in London spot gold prices. Central bank benchmark prices were even lower. However, the unchanged exchange rate of shillings to US dollars increased selling pressure and led to a decline. Market conditions returned to a state of slackness. Early in the morning, news from overseas silver markets indicated that the UK market contracted while the US market remained flat. Large traders said that after the market closed, sellers were following the benchmark prices, causing market fatigue. The forward silver price in Montreux contracted by eight hao. Exchange rates continued to rise. London pure gold prices fell by five pence. The central bank's benchmark prices were announced, with both the UK and US markets flat. Customs gold unit prices fell by four li. The benchmark price for gold bars fell further to 1117.8 yuan. Off-market pre-trading opened, falling to within 25 yuan, then briefly rising to above 6 yuan. However, at this point, there was a lack of formal transactions, leading to a chaotic situation. Later, with Dah Đức Cheng and Wǔ Chāng Xiáng selling, the price fell to 4.5 yuan, and the situation stabilized slightly. The morning opened with low prices. After opening, supply and demand balanced out, and prices rose and fell briefly on the market, but the range was limited. Later, short sellers took the opportunity to exert pressure, gradually pushing prices down. There were still spot buyers taking advantage of the low prices, providing some support. However, because the exchange rates announced by the banks were flat for both the UK and US, and the silver equalization tax contracted by two-fifths, buying sentiment never really picked up. Although there was a rebound later in the session, it was mostly sideways movement. The overall trend turned mediocre, and the market became even more stable later. The morning session was slightly weak, and the afternoon gradually rebounded. Both the first and second reports on Indian silver were flat, and the market returned to a state of slackness at the end. The day's market conditions are recorded below:

The morning opened at 1125 yuan, down two yuan from the previous close. Qià Fēng Yǒng advanced from 4.7 to 5.2 yuan. Chéng Dà, Dah Đức Cheng, Héng Yú, Yuán Mào, and Yǒng shed holdings, falling back to 4.1 yuan. Shēng Yuán Yǒng, Qià Fēng Yǒng still took in, rising to 4.8 yuan. HSBC's benchmark prices were flat for both the UK and US, and the silver equalization tax was reduced by two-fifths. Dah Đức Cheng and Fú Xīng Yǒng shed holdings, falling to 4.3 yuan. Shēng Yuán Yǒng, Yuán Mào Yǒng, and Dà Chāng Xiáng maintained at the low price, and then rebounded to 4.9 yuan, making the sideways trend even more apparent. Cross-trading was sparse. The morning session closed at 1124.7 yuan.

The afternoon market opened at 1124.3 yuan. Qià Fēng Yǒng and Fú Tài Yǒng sold strips, falling back to 4.2 yuan. Tóng Tài Chāng, Dah Đức Cheng, and others took in, while Yuán Mào Yǒng and others also added to their positions, rising to 4.9 yuan. Fú Xīng Yǒng, Dah Đức Cheng, and others limited sales at the higher price. The session closed at 1124.7 yuan.

The closing price was benchmarked against the central bank's standard gold bar price, falling to 1117.8 yuan. Speaking in terms of closing prices, it was raised approximately seven yuan. The current month's registered price is 1122 yuan, and October's is 1125 yuan. The morning's water top-up was 1122 yuan. The price of red gold was increased by 13.5 yuan, and boiled red gold was increased by 15 yuan. However, there were no buyers. The selling price was increased by 12 yuan, but there were no transactions.

Trading within the market returned to a flat state. In summary, Shēng Yuán Yǒng, Tóng Tài Chāng, Dà Chāng Xiáng, Huì Xiáng, Yuán Mào Yǒng, Wàn Xīng, and others were on the buying side, while Dah Đức Cheng, Qìng Fā Yǒng, Chéng Dà, Héng Yú Xiáng Fēng, Fú Tài Yǒng, Jiǔ Dà Rùn Chāng, and Yù Xiáng Hé were on the selling side. Qià Fēng Yǒng advanced first and then exited.

The day's market conditions were flat and weak. The morning opened at 1125 yuan, and the final closing price was 1124.7 yuan. The highest price was 1125.2 yuan, and the lowest price was 1124.1 yuan, a difference of 1.1 yuan. The closing price fell 2.3 yuan from the previous close. There were still 672 strips left in the current month's forwards. In total, there were nine long positions and five short positions. For the October futures contracts, there were a total of 8610 strips, with 29 long positions and 41 short positions. The total number of transactions was 1120 strips in the morning session and 238 strips in the afternoon session.

The prospects for trading are particularly difficult to develop. Therefore, the range of market price fluctuations is bound to be very narrow. Yesterday's activity, during both morning sessions, was slightly weak. Numbers 47 and 53 were sold, while Number 11 was bought, and Number 16 also saw some buying. Trading in both afternoon sessions was even quieter, and market conditions tended to be chaotic, with a sense of uncertainty. The absence of securities trading in this kind of environment must have a reason. There is not much hope for the future. The final market price results showed a slight decrease of 0.15 to 0.25. The cotton market is stable. Although American cotton has fallen back, Indian cotton has surged. Cotton prices in Zhengzhou, Yujin, and other places have risen, and people's confidence is growing. As a result, new selling is increasingly rare, and the market situation is still returning, but the weather is gradually clearing, and cotton fields are benefiting greatly.

New Short Positions Seem to Have Decreased Slightly

The opening of the spot cotton market saw Indian cotton surging, with Robbie up by half to 6.5 Robbie. However, the previous day's soaring American cotton fell back by 14 pounds, and Osaka's Sanpin cotton fell by 0.1 to 0.3 jiao. The weather gradually improved, and the market became ordinary. American Cotton Rises Too Quickly, Causes Reaction

Yesterday, American cotton opened with a rise of 0.4 to 0.7 pounds for each month. Early in the morning, Liverpool's news was strong, and traders, brokers, and foreign merchants all bought in. Soon after, the market price rose too quickly, causing some hesitation, and selling increased, with longs settling positions, causing a market reaction. However, demand from traders was still good, and near-term shorts were covering positions. Most of the current demand was to settle old positions. Factory buyers were average, and textiles were firm and active. The close was flat and weak, with spot prices falling by 0.4 pounds and futures prices falling by 0.4 to 1.2 pounds. English spot cotton rose by 39 points, and futures rose or fell by 1 point. A large number of longs on Indian cotton took profits and manipulators sold, which was absorbed by European exporters and futures traders. After that, cotton merchants cross-bought to meet long settlements. Nagpur rose by 2.25 rupees, Oomra rose by 4.75 rupees, and Broach rose by 6.5 rupees. Shortage of Spot Piece Goods and Cotton Cloth, Autumn Clearance Sale on This Street is Booming, Purchasing Power in the Yangtze River Basin Increases, Sales are Active

Yesterday, the yarn and cotton markets were stable, and the cotton cloth market continued to be strong. After continuous large movements, inventory was short. 16-pound and 14-pound coarse cloth, after being purchased in large quantities by military units and the Tianjin gang, the market's bottom was depleted. Each stall expressed a lack of it, and the market price rose by 0.05 to 0.1 yuan per piece. Mainland gangs were the most eager to purchase. Stores on this street started an autumn clearance sale yesterday with greatly reduced prices, drawing crowded customers and booming business. Various ports along the Yangtze River, due to this year's abundant harvest, had slightly increased purchasing power, and sales of various goods were active. Pre-ordered patterned goods, printed velvet from various factories, Zhigong, Serge, line cloth, were shipped upon arrival every day. White goods, fine cloth, fine twill, were still being vigorously purchased by the Yue and Gui gangs, with over 400 additional pieces sold yesterday. After Tianjin gangs purchased large quantities of coarse cloth and coarse twill, they have been shipping in batches for days. The Dian gang purchased over 200 pieces of Hongzhang Factory's Three Sheep Zhigong, Serge, Meiheng Factory's crepe ne, Zhigong satin, line cloth, Guanghua, Renfeng Factory's Shilin cloth, this factory's fine cloth, coarse twill, Hengfeng Factory's Lao Hua Gong ne and other goods. Zhigong and Serge from Chinese factories, affected by the rising price of Dong goods "Four Gentlemen," also increased in price by 0.005 yuan per meter, it is said.

Little Demand for Harris Tweed

Harris Tweed, following Xiangshui Ne, was once popular. Later, because of its cheap price, buyers disliked it. The spring wholesale price suddenly rose this year, so people thought it was too expensive and avoided it. This autumn, the price of Harris Tweed is even more expensive. Ordinary goods are sold at 5.5 yuan, and low-end goods also require 4.6 to 4.7 yuan. As a result, buyers dare not take it. They only cut samples and try to sell them to customers first. However, customers find it too hairy and not soft, so there is little demand, leading to sluggish sales.

Passenger Sales Gradually Increase, Yuanfang's Prices Increase, Do Not Decrease

Yesterday, Thursday, was the 3006th auction of Yuanfang Foreign Firm. The goods displayed included Taixi satin, yuan velvet, Zhigong ne, Yugang foreign red cloth, a total of five types, 61 boxes of 46 brands. Patterned foreign yarn, poplin, foreign blue cloth, and bleached fine cloth, which were previously available, were not included because there were no goods arriving from overseas. Customers from various roads and gangs were active, and prices were higher than the previous period for each brand. Taixi satin was sold at 6 brands, increasing by about 0.01 yuan per meter. Yuan velvet at 2 brands increased by about 0.02 yuan each. Zhigong ne rose by 0.03 yuan. In Yuyu silk, there were 37 brands, including the Tongbao Sandingjia brand that had not been available for a long time, and industry members competed to buy it. The other brands mostly increased in price, with Weiluweixiao Xinshang Zhongqiu Denggao Jiulian Deng 4 brand each rising 0.5 yuan per piece, and the rest each rose 0.2 or 0.3 yuan, except for Kuailitu, which rose in price during the previous call, now decreased by 0.05 yuan. The price of four-weight red cloth is still strong, it is said.

Food: Flour Near Months Rise, Far Months Fall

Yesterday's flour market, after the morning opening, presented a tired and then stable trend. According to foreign wheat quotations, Chicago was down 0.001 yuan, and Canada was down 0.002 to 0.003 yuan. When prices opened, the weather turned sunny, and foreign wheat saw a slight decline, so prices at the opening were flat. November and below, due to long exits and factory hedging, had fallen back by about 0.015 yuan. However, off-market longs then took in again, causing each subsequent session to gradually recover. By the afternoon opening, although there were few transactions in the current month, the market atmosphere was tight due to floating shorts covering. Although sales were not smooth, outside firms still held on. The long-term mentality was different, and although outside firms bought in, sellers also flooded in, presenting a fluctuating trend. The future situation will depend on whether actual sales can continue, and then the market will return to the right path, it is said.

Metals Domestic Copper Sheet Prices Continue to Rise

Domestic copper sheets have seen a significant price surge recently. This is mainly due to the shortage of old copper raw materials plaguing various factories, leading to scarce production. The market demand exceeds supply, causing successive increases in standard prices. Currently, the market price is 52-53 yuan per dan, an increase of 2-3 yuan compared to the previous period. Compared to this time last year, the price has soared by about 10 yuan. It's also noted that thermos bottle factories are actively seeking supplies. Consequently, factories are actively searching for raw materials from Hong Kong and inland regions.

Yangtze Route

Ming Xing 1

Wheat Price Re-enters Stability After Fatigue

Yesterday, the wheat market opened steadily in the morning, but then weakened for each month. It then showed signs of rebounding. Initially, although there was a slight decrease in foreign wheat, the market sentiment was mostly cautious. Therefore, the asking price was similar to the previous day. Later, due to the pullback of long positions and the lack of new buyers, the price fell by one or two points. However, when the market opened in the afternoon, transactions for each month were still active. Because the flour market rebounded and stabilized, the asking price for spot wheat also increased by one or two points, causing market sentiment for each month to re-enter stability. According to the current actual situation, the wheat market is inevitably expensive, and flour sales will naturally decrease invisibly. Therefore, insiders generally believe that although international changes are unpredictable, speculators may still take advantage of them. In the spot wheat market, high-quality wheat is asking for one or two points higher, while medium and lower quality wheat remains unchanged. Wuhe wheat is priced at $4.95, second-grade at $4.52, Guzhen wheat at $4.92, Wuyi wheat at $4.80, Zhuzhen wheat at $4.79, Gaoyou wheat at $4.75, second-grade at $4.73, Hushu wheat at $4.75, Nanjing wheat at $4.70, Tuqian wheat at $4.87, second-grade at $4.85, and Yanghe wheat at $4.92, and Zhenjiang wheat at $4.64. Fuxin and Fufeng each handled 3,000 bags, and Shenda handled 2,000 bags.

Flour Mill Sesame Trading Resumes Vigorously - Enquiries from British, Japanese and Italian Merchants, Industry Insiders Also Replenishing at Low Prices

The dumping and trading of foreign-grown new sesame seeds is trending towards vitality again. Due to inquiries from British, Japanese, and Italian merchants, and some industry insiders taking advantage of the low prices to counter short positions, the market atmosphere suddenly became tight, and the price was able to rise immediately. The previous night, Dafo and Heyi foreign firms handled 450 tons for October and November delivery, priced at $11.85. Yesterday, a Japanese firm handled 200 tons for delivery within this month, priced at $12.20. Jardine Matheson and others handled 300 tons for delivery in October and November, priced at $12.00.

Prices for Thick Japonica Rice and Thin Indica Rice Remain Stable

(South Shanghai) Yesterday, the source of goods from various groups was still only Nos. 12 and 13, with a total of more than 2,000 shih (石). However, both retail and wholesale markets were sluggish, making it difficult for the market to rebound. Prices for thick early japonica rice and thin indica rice remained unchanged. Dongxin japonica rice was also similar, with factory and riverfront prices being flat. New high-quality rice from Yangchuan and other places showed no fluctuations, and the price of “Yinbian Yuan” rice also lacked ups and downs.

(North Shanghai) Yesterday, riverfront goods arriving were around No. 20. Various types of rice on the market were being consumed, with some transactions occurring for broken japonica rice, Dongxin japonica rice, old and new Yangjian rice, and new Yangtuanjian rice at lower prices. Sales of Xinbu Jian rice were slightly improved, and high-quality Yinbian Yuan rice was still active, while thin indica rice and new Kejian rice were average. Market prices for broken japonica rice were firm, while prices for new and old Yangjian rice and Dongxin japonica rice were flat and weak. The price of Xinbu Jian rice was slightly lower by two cents, high-quality Yinbian Yuan rice was firm, while medium and lower quality rice was weak. The price of new Tuankejian rice was reduced by a few cents.

Decline in Kexian Rice Prices Triggers Cantonese Sales

Yesterday, there were continued new arrivals of nearly 10,000 bags of Kexian rice, and sales of the local Kexian rice also reached 15,000 bags. However, with continuous arrivals in recent days, inventories have gradually increased. Due to the suspension of shipments by the Guangdong group for several days, there was more accumulation on the market. Traders and owners were all eager to sell. After the Guangdong group resumed shipments the day before yesterday, owners were quite willing to reduce prices to sell. Yesterday, the market saw a small decline of five or six cents. Sales were mainly to Guangdong, with approximately 7,000 bags of Shahan brown rice, Hunan broken rice, rice milled by machine in brown rice form, and Anqing rice being sold. Shantou also took 3,000 bags of Xianggan rice milled by machine in brown rice form, while the rest was sold by the local market.

Silk and Tea - Poor Autumn Harvest in Japan, Local Silk Market Gradually Improving

For more than ten days, the foreign silk market can be said to have been declining daily. However, since the news of the poor autumn harvest in Japan was announced, market sentiment has gradually become firm. As of yesterday, the silk markets in New York and New York showed a unanimous increase. It is estimated that 83 and 75 degrees of Japanese silk in New York each rose by three points, while Shanghai silk and Guangdong silk each rose by one point. Standard silk rose by four points for the near term and one and a half points for the long term. Spot goods rose by two to eight yuan, but Lyon did not show any changes. The silk market in Shanghai has seen healthy sales from various user groups, resulting in more stable prices than in previous days. Yesterday also saw a rebound. The foreign pure market is also gradually approaching, with Dachang and Bira and others having considerable purchasing interest. User sales are no longer quiet. If Yokohama silk prices can gradually become firm, then this local area will

Qihong Tea is Planning a Complete Sale

This year, the combined flower fragrance yield of Qimen, Fuliang, Zhizhi, and Ningzhou black tea is estimated to be 100,000 boxes. As of the current market, more than 8,800 boxes of Qining black tea flower fragrance have been sold, with varying qualities. Although British firms such as Xiehe, Jardine Matheson, and Jinlong have continued to replenish their stocks, it is not easy to clear the inventory. In view of this, the Anhui-Jiangxi Black Tea General Transportation and Sales Office plans to seek a complete sale plan and has ordered the Quality Assessment Committee to estimate the quality for review.

Xilu Tea Baitou Firms Resume Purchasing

According to the report from the Tea Shop Association, the green tea market still lacks large-scale transactions. In recent days, foreign firms have achieved some retail success with core-pulled Zhenmei teas, with Baochang and Tongfu each purchasing over 100 boxes and Tianxiang and Huacha each purchasing dozens of boxes at prices ranging from 90 to 112 yuan. Jinlong only has an appetite for Xiaozhenmei tea, purchasing approximately 250 boxes at prices of 22 to 23 yuan. Furthermore, Baitou firms have recently resumed purchasing Gongxi tea, with prices several yuan lower than before, approximately 22 to 23 yuan, resulting in over 400 boxes being traded. Approximately 700 boxes of Pingshui Zhenmei tea were purchased by Huacha at prices of 25 to 27 yuan.

The Necessary Movement for New Poets

— Lei Shiyu

In recent years, the Chinese poetry scene has indeed become much more vibrant, but in reality, there hasn’t been a phenomenon of “poetry publications and new poetry collections springing up like bamboo shoots after rain.” Taking Shanghai, the so-called hub of culture, as an example, there are no more than two or three poetry magazines, and instead of flourishing briefly, they seem to be in a criminal trial, never showing their face a second time. The new poetry collections that appear in a year are also only a few and very thin. Only in newspapers and general literary publications do poetry works often occupy some space. On the surface, it seems quite lively, but it is only relatively lively because it depends on the prosperity of general literary magazines. However, looking at the entire poetry scene, one cannot help but say that it is still shrouded in gloom.

The fact that there isn't a single regular poetry magazine in all of China is naturally due to the lack of organization among Chinese poets. Therefore, their activities also lack the strength of a group, and their creative practice lacks planning and unity.

If Chinese poets do not respond to the torrent of this troubled era by uniting and developing widely, even if we have the reality to provide us with great works, we will be overwhelmed by reality.

I am not against organizations such as "Poets' Clubs," but I am extremely opposed if they only take the form of a group of a few people! What we should advocate now and put into practice as soon as possible is the creation of a "Chinese Poetry Association." Only by establishing the front line of Chinese poetry in this unified, planned, universal, and connected way can the poetry movement develop strongly and effectively.

The Chinese publishing industry is terrible, especially with its continued neglect of poetry. Not only is there not a single bookstore willing to publish a dedicated poetry magazine, but even when a literary publication signs a distribution contract with the boss, it is often based on the premise of how many established masters are writing for the magazine. Editors also often hold onto idol worship or the common ills of "feudal systemism, dividing personnel and dividing art." Even worse, many old tyrants use magazines as a means of commercial profiteering and even deception.

In a publishing industry full of scams, coupled with the lack of security for writers' lives, the lack of certainty in publishing, and the lack of freedom in creative activities, the lack of cultural development is by no means accidental. This is often the result of the complex relationships formed by China's social, political, and economic factors and their interpenetration. However, the lack of organization among writers and the lack of a unified fighting front is also a major reason.

Without mutual criticism and encouragement, and without constant efforts, now, along with the unfolding of the tense world situation and the rapid changes in Chinese society, our literary artists consciously join hands and work hard for new poetry.

Poetry is a branch of art, and it is also the earliest art to emerge in mankind, and it has always been called the "King of Literature." However, this "King of Literature" is still like a "literary lackey" in our Chinese literary scene, but we do not want to establish a "kingdom" for it, but rather to make it a powerful trumpet in the struggle for national liberation!

Donkey

— Wei Dongming

"Is your animal well-behaved?"

That was the first time I rode a donkey. It was in the spring of this year when I happened to take a walk outside the school gate. Several donkey drivers surrounded me, soliciting business. Out of curiosity and the fact that I was bored, I agreed on a price with a middle-aged donkey driver with pockmarks on his face and decided to ride to the city gate. Knowing that there wouldn't be any danger, but because it was the first time, I was a little scared and asked that question, worried about encountering a stubborn and wild animal that would throw me off. The pockmarked man, while answering that the donkey had a very good temperament, walked down the dirt slope and untied the rope tethering the donkey from the wooden stake. When he pulled the rope uphill, the donkey braced its legs and refused to move, pulling its mouth crooked but still struggling not to take a step until the donkey driver whipped its back twice with the end of the rope, and only then did it lazily saunter up the dirt slope. This situation increased my doubts:

"Your donkey is probably too stubborn."

"It doesn't matter, the animal just gets lazy when it rests, just like people. Don't worry, you can get on." The pockmarked donkey driver replied like this, his smile making people feel that he was kind and reliable. He had the donkey stop by the side of the road, straightened the saddle, tightened the girth, and then helped me onto the donkey's back, helping me insert my feet into the stirrups. Seeing that I had pulled up the reins and was sitting upright on the saddle, he walked to the front, pulling a section of iron chain tied to the donkey's left cheek strap, shouted, and the donkey started to walk.

When I first got on the donkey and only took a few steps, I was very nervous, my nerves were alert at all times. After walking a distance, I gradually calmed down. But just when I was about to relax a little, the donkey, upon reaching the main road, struggled to walk down a small path leading to the professor's residential area of the school. I quickly regained my composure, returned to a state of tension, and instructed the donkey driver to lead the animal back onto the original road. He told me that if I wanted the animal to turn in a certain direction, I just had to pull the reins on that side tightly. Then he explained that in the professor's residential area down that small path, there were several young students who often rode donkeys for fun. The donkey was familiar with this place, so without waiting for anyone to say anything, it walked onto that path.

I had the donkey driver continue to walk beside me, pulling the chain on the left side of the donkey's head, walking as slowly as possible. In order to pass the time and conceal the fact that the donkey was walking too slowly, I began to look for some things to chat about with him.

"Where do you live?"

"Just east of the garden, in the village next to the railway."

"What is your surname?"

"It's an honor for you to ask, my humble surname is Li."

Then he asked me my surname, and I told him.

"How many people are in your family?"

"Five, two adults, three children."

"No elderly?"

"They've all passed away."

"The three children are all yours, how many boys and girls are there?"

"They're all mine, three girls."

"It would be nice to have a boy, are they all in school?"

"You're right, but how can we afford to send them to school?"

"Doesn't the university in the garden have a public school? Free schooling, doesn't cost money."

"But the family doesn't even have two decent meals a day, and we don't have clothes to wear out. At home, they can also take on some odd jobs, collect some wild vegetables for the family to eat."

"Have you always made a living by driving a donkey?"

"Originally, my parents had more than ten acres of land, but with donations and taxes, and several years of famine, it was borrowed and mortgaged. When I took over, all that was left was a small donkey for grinding grain."

"Who was the land mortgaged to?"

"Who else but the big landlords on the ground? The land deed was mortgaged to them for money, and if you can't pay it back, it belongs to them."

At this time, the donkey had already walked onto the rural dirt road parallel to the railway. In front of a small coal factory near the station, a small coal truck was parked loading goods, and the donkey driving that truck was also facing the dirt road we were walking on. It raised its neck and began to bray at us. The donkey I was riding also raised its head and brayed at it, and kicked its hind legs, trying to run towards the coal factory. The conversation had to be temporarily suspended. I gripped the reins tightly, somewhat frightened, imagining what posture I should fall in so that I wouldn't get hurt so badly. The pockmarked man was not flustered at all, and very skillfully pulled the iron chain to lower the donkey's head, pressing it to make it stop on the road for a while before leading it slowly forward again. He told me not to panic, not to be afraid, this was common; when a donkey sees another donkey on the road, both of them will bray, just like when we people meet on the road, we will greet each other and say, "Where are you going?" Listening to these words, the panic-stricken beating of my heart had returned to normal, and I found his words rather naive and funny. I also thought about asking him if either of the donkeys was a female, and he said they were both male donkeys, female donkeys don't bray.

The conversation then turned from people to donkeys. The pockmarked donkey driver boasted that his donkey was stable and reliable and would not throw people off its back. Moreover—

"You're a beginner, but people who ride often specifically want fast ones. Running down from the Eight Great Sites of the Western Hills, forty or fifty li in one breath, running all the way to the destination, the person can't get off the donkey, the donkey is covered in sweat, and the donkey's legs and belly are trembling when it stands, wow, that's really!..."

"Then how do you keep up?" I interjected.

"Of course, I also run right behind, and if I can't keep up, I chase after it from a distance!"

In this way, just as he said, the more I rode, the bolder I became, so I told him that he didn't need to lead in front, he could just follow behind and drive the donkey a little faster. In fact, the road ahead was sandwiched between cornfields and could no longer allow a person and a donkey to pass through side by side with ease. He agreed and taught me again, if I wanted the donkey to stop, I just had to pull the rein back tightly and shout "Whoa, whoa..." and it wouldn't go. As he said this, he went around to the back of the donkey, shouting out another kind of sound, and the donkey quickened its pace, trotting down the dirt road. It kicked up the dust beside me, and this dust surrounded the donkey's hooves like yellow smoke.

A slight breeze brushed against my face, and as I rode on the donkey's back, bumping up and down, I felt a lightness that I didn't feel when walking slowly. Behind me, I heard the donkey driver's footsteps as he ran along, accompanied by the gradually louder panting.

As we went on like this, the donkey occasionally raised its head to look up. Thinking that it was going to bray and kick again, I pulled the reins and shouted "Whoa, whoa," and the donkey stopped.

"What's wrong? There aren't any of its buddies ahead, why is it acting up again?" I turned back and asked the donkey driver.

"It doesn't matter," he came up and stroked the donkey's hindquarters and belly with his hand: "It raises its head to look at the old man, to see what time it is."

He then shouted again, and the animal started running again. In this simple action, I saw that he had not only a deep understanding of this animal but also an unlimited affection for it.

Turning from the suburban dirt road to the main road, the city gate was already in sight.

Since that donkey ride, I haven't ridden again. A few days ago, when I walked out of the school gate, preparing to go into the city, several donkey drivers and rickshaw pullers surrounded me again, soliciting business. Although I hadn't seen the face of the previous donkey driver, Lao Li, clearly because he was only on the side or behind me all the way, I was sure I recognized his pockmarks. One of the people surrounding me this time had a familiar pockmarked face. I said to him:

"Aren't you Lao Li? I'm not riding a donkey this time."

Seeing that I recognized him, he seemed a little happy, and he stepped back and pulled a rickshaw out from among the row of parked rickshaws and placed it in front of me, unexpectedly:

"Hehe, get in the car, where do you want to go, pay as you see fit."

I got into the car and asked:

"Lao Li, did you sell the donkey and buy a rickshaw?"

He replied:

"Hehe, the rickshaw is rented."

A Certain Bank

— TK

The Witch's Home

— Yin Guang

My landlady is a witch. When I first found this house, I was satisfied with all aspects, especially the cheap rent. But when I learned that the hall below was a place for offering sacrifices to gods, with plaques like "Always Responsive" and "Sincerity Brings Miracles" hanging all around, I hesitated. Other things didn't matter much, but my first concern was that too many people would come to burn incense, which would inevitably disturb my peace. Secondly, I was afraid she was worshipping a fox spirit, because, according to what others told me, these creatures are very petty. If you say something even slightly wrong, they will immediately play tricks on you. Although I am not superstitious, living with such a thing day and night would be very annoying. So I asked the old woman who was dealing with me – I later learned that she was the witch.

"What kind of Bodhisattva do you worship?"

She replied, "It's Madam Lü Chunyang."

I couldn't help but smile. "Are there many people who burn incense?"

"Not many, not many. You'll know after living here for a while." She seemed to see that I was afraid of the noise and hurriedly waved her hand as she answered.

Since she was not worshipping a fox spirit and wouldn't be noisy, I decided to move in. Now I have lived here for nearly three months, and I am very familiar with the family's life, and I even feel a sense of leisurely interest in them.

There are six people in their family: an old couple, two sons, and two daughters. The whole family are genuine farmers, as if a long life in the city has had no impact on them.

The old man is about forty or fifty years old, but he is very healthy. He is tall and thin, with a small head, graying hair, and small, deep-set eyes. However, with a small, pointed nose, his appearance is not too unpleasant. His voice is very loud, and he usually sounds like he is arguing when he talks to people. When I first moved in, because I didn't have a suitable place to put a mop, I temporarily placed it at the entrance of the stairs. When he saw it, he used his big throat to argue with the friend who was helping me move. My friend was so scared that he didn't dare to speak. I thought, "This is terrible! How come I didn't see such an old man when I looked at the house that day?"

Now I understand that he was born with such a voice, and he is not intentionally arguing with anyone. However, it is enough to make people suffer.

He plants flowers for a foreigner.

He loves to be greedy for small advantages. Even a piece of rusty wire is good for him. He often brings back many things from the foreigner, such as green paint, white paint, tung oil, and lime. These things are all contained in cigarette tins or other cans, carefully wrapped in newspapers, and carefully carried back. In the afternoon, when he has nothing to do, he picks up a can of paint and either paints the door green or the window white. You always see him painting non-stop. Therefore, the house is painted with patches of green, white, and black, making it look a mess. I think it might look good in his eyes. There are fresh flowers offered in front of their gods every day, which, needless to say, the old man brought back. He is very afraid of his wife – the witch. Whenever she is unhappy, or when he is talking loudly to someone, his wife lowers her face and says to him:

"What are you yapping about again?" Then he will run off to do something without saying a word. Naturally, he goes back to his painting.

The whole family is very frugal, eating very poorly, and dressing very poorly. The old man often says to others:

"Don't look at some people who dress very well? In truth, they can't even pay the rent."

Their eldest son is an apprentice in a leather shoe store and is the only handsome person in the family. He seems to have little connection with the family. He only comes back to sleep every night and leaves again at dawn.

The second son is a high school student in elementary school, about to graduate. Strangely, he doesn't show any dissatisfaction with his mother's business. He spends his summer vacation playing with cicadas with other children and helping his mother start the fire when cooking. I haven't seen him touch a single book. He is not young, sixteen or seventeen years old, and looks very tall. Once, I asked his mother:

"After he graduates from elementary school, does he plan to study further?"

"No, he won't study anymore. Don't you see those middle school students next door who have been idle at home for a long time? I don't have that much money to pay for his studies." She said with indignation.

She continued:

"My Gengdi can attend school because Guang Sheng agreed to only charge half the fee, for half a year in total." She also mentioned the reason why her second daughter went to school.

The second daughter is a spoiled child of seven or eight years old who has been spoiled, and cannot even distinguish between male and female teachers, as for the words in the books, she doesn't recognize a single one, but she can read very well along with others.

The eldest daughter looks very much like her mother, especially her big eyes with long, black eyelashes, which makes her look like a cunning spirit. However, her pale white face and her completely bony body are far inferior to those of her parents. She works in a cigarette factory, earning one and a half cents for packing enough cigarettes, but even such cheap work is not available every day. She mostly goes once every other day, or even faces long-term unemployment of more than a month.

Now I will talk about the main figure in this family – the witch. Judging from her appearance alone, she does not look as frighteningly strange as the average witch, and is not much different from an ordinary old woman in her forties or fifties. She is short and slightly plump, with black hair, large eyes, and long, black eyelashes. Her eyes blink very quickly when she speaks, and you can tell at a glance that she is a formidable old woman. Her right ankle is thicker than her left, and she doesn't walk very easily. She can heal people and scare away evil spirits from children. She relies on her Bodhisattva to heal adults and her own experience to heal children. Her business is not bad, and people often come to ask for fortunes. The prescriptions are printed on the fortune slips. As for how much money to give, it is up to the patient. I think this income is very limited. The main income comes from healing children's diseases, as people are willing to pay more for their own children. She doesn't have a set time; she sees people as they come, and it usually costs four or five cents each time. It is said that she can also get two or three yuan for a house call. Once, I saw her pick white spots from an infant's mouth with my own eyes. She calmly took out a needle more than an inch long from the medicine box, without sterilizing it. She opened the infant's mouth with one hand and put the needle in with the other, picking with a popping sound. Blood flowed out along her fingers, and the infant cried so hard that it lost its voice. The mother turned her head away and dared not look again. But she was still calmly picking, with no expression on her face, as if she were picking on a piece of wood. After the procedure was completed, she used a metal tube, placing a little white powder on one end and blowing it into the infant's mouth. When the other person left, they slipped a small roll of corner tickets into her hand, and she smiled, saying:

"Don't be polite!" As she slowly put it into her pocket.

Their Bodhisattva is kept in a glass box. Once, I asked her eldest daughter to open it for me to see, and she seriously refused:

"I can't open it!"

"Why not?" I asked strangely.

"We have to wait for my mother to come. She has fairy bones, and the Bodhisattva won't blame her." So I asked her where their "Madam Lü Chunyang" came from. She generously told me the reason why they worship the god: "We didn't worship gods before. Three years ago, my mother was sick in bed and couldn't move. My father was also sick and even vomited blood! One night, the Bodhisattva possessed my mother and told her to worship her because she had fairy bones. If we believed in her, their illnesses would get better. Later, they really got better. She also healed many other people."

"Then where did you get the Bodhisattva from?" I said, pointing to the idol.

She replied calmly, "We bought it in the city."

"Can Bodhisattvas be bought with money?" I almost shouted! But in reality, I vaguely said, "Hmm!" and mumbled past it.

This old woman doesn't have any other illnesses, except that she has a red erysipelas on her particularly thick right ankle, which flares up two or three times a month. When it flares up, she can't walk a single step and can only lie down, emitting terrible groans, and her husband, who likes to quarrel, also temporarily becomes mute.

Today I Pay My Respects to Esthetes at Bai Causeway

— Dabao

Today’s hurried journey,

Leaves my footprints on the Bai Causeway of West Lake.

I come here to seek the harmony of heaven,

To admire the resting place of the souls of esthetes.

Strolling in the wind on Bai Causeway,

I recall the ancient poets along the way—

They sang of sacred peace,

Sang of the beautiful spring,

The love of youth…

They gained the worship of later generations of men and women,

With immortal poems.

I pay my respects to all esthetes,

They represent the most noble souls of mankind,

They spread the song of happiness to the present and future generations—

First, I pay my respects to Bai Juyi,

He opposed war and sang of peace;

I pay my respects to Su Manshu,

He sang of transcending the world to relieve suffering;

I pay my respects to Su Xiaoxiao and Feng Xiaoqing,

Their lives themselves are moving songs.

Poets of peace,

Gallant courtesans,

After death, you rest forever by the beautiful lake,

Considered to have found the realm you sang of.

However, I want to, in the name of a reader,

Ask your peaceful tombs—

Is the tomb the final destination

Of the names of all ideals?

West Lake has tranquil waves,

The lakeside has gentle breezes and willows,

Ancient poets rest under the shade of the trees,

Modern tourists wander under the shade of the trees,

They come here to escape the noise of the city.

In the city, in the mortal world,

Humanity has lost its beauty and harmony.

Today, it is still a chaotic world!

We live under the butcher's knife;

Groups of unfortunate humans,

No one can escape the present world

They encounter hunger, suffering, and slaughter;

Hold back on singing about youth and love,

Everywhere is etiquette, conspiracy, and depravity!

Today I pay my respects to all esthetes at Bai Causeway,

Tomorrow,

Tomorrow the express train will take me back through the wilderness to the city of sin.

The Place to Die

— Qin Wen

The newspaper reported that a male coolie around forty years old, suffering from illness and without a place to stay, slept at night in a cement tile pipe placed by the Public Works Department on the open space of Route Massenet in the French Concession, and died of serious illness in the tile pipe. Mr. Neng Gong believed that "some people will see this corpse as a symbol of human barbarism and shame," and considered him a "silent witness."

After working hard all his life, he didn't even have a place to lie down and die properly, and had to secretly collapse in a tile pipe, which is sad enough. But there are coolies who die even more tragically; it is said that just last month, on the slope of the Jimei Wharf, there was a person lying there, so thin that there were only bones inside the skin. Presumably, he intended to take the Tongmei bus back to his hometown, but he was so sick that he couldn't walk or speak well; just as the tide was rising, the seawater soaked his body, and he勉强爬向岸边,勉强爬了一些路就停止了.潮水又涨到,才再爬一下。The tide rose again, and he would crawl a little further. To prevent the stench, they carried him to Xiamen, also on the wharf. The next day the tide rose again, but he still didn't die,苟延残喘,苟延残喘,苟延残喘,于是又这样：潮涨一点，他爬一下；再涨一点，再爬一下。脚是任凭浸着的，总要海水滚上了大腿，他才拚命挣扎。Compared to this, dying in the tile pipe seems better, as it would be quieter.

If you can still walk, you have to look for a tile pipe to die in. For people without a home to return to, tile pipes are worth paying attention to at all times!

Seeing such records and hearing such news, I am very surprised. This is not accidental; seven years ago, Yuan Qing rented a house in Yu Lou. Because the expo was about to open, Yu Lou could no longer be lived in, so he had to move to Ge Ling. It was expensive and far away, with many inconveniences, so he had to move again, squeezing into a small building in Guanghua Temple, which was extremely hot and stuffy. He became seriously ill and had no choice but to move to the school where I taught. It made me deeply feel that there was really no place to be sick and no place to die.

He had made many contributions in art, but it seemed that suffering was to be expected for things like painting.

Tile pipe! Is it really a destination?
